Current Affairs Commentary

Concerning the Saar Region's Return to Germany 26

By Heng

According to recent foreign dispatches, the Saar plebiscite has concluded with a victory for Germany, securing 477,119 votes. This outcome aligns with our expectations. The League of Nations has governed the Saar for fifteen years, and its measures, broadly speaking, have been quite enlightened. Freedoms such as assembly, association, education, language, writing, nationality, and religion have generally been respected. For a region governed by others, this level of freedom is, objectively speaking, a reasonably satisfactory form of governance. However, the voting results show that this region will ultimately return to Germany. This is primarily due to the paramount importance of national sentiment. Every nation in the world desires independence and autonomy. Being governed by others, no matter how enlightened or fortunate, is ultimately perceived as a great humiliation in the national consciousness. Therefore, the Saar's return to Germany is an inevitable fact and not surprising.

Previously, some international affairs analysts speculated that, given the German political situation, the Saar plebiscite might maintain the status quo. Their reasoning was based on the fact that since Hitler came to power in Germany, many dissidents had fled to the Saar. Furthermore, Catholics constituted a significant majority in the Saar, and their feelings towards Hitler were not amicable. If they collectively voted to maintain the status quo, the overall outcome would be uncertain. However, these German exiles advocating for maintaining the status quo, as well as the Socialists and Communists, constituted only a minority of the population. Secondly, the Catholic Church, through repeated notices from the Pope, instructed followers not to let religious grievances interfere with their conscientious choices. Therefore, there was no anti-German propaganda campaign. At the same time, Catholics feared that if Germany failed, they would be blamed and retaliated against, so they were even less inclined to support the anti-German faction. With Catholics abandoning their stance of maintaining the status quo, the Saar's return to Germany was never in question.

The Saar's return to Germany is now procedurally complete. The remaining issues to be resolved are: (1) How to raise funds to reclaim the mineral resources in the area; (2) How to protect those in the region who advocated for maintaining the status quo. These two issues were partially addressed in the Franco-German agreement of December 3rd of last year. The former issue involves Germany raising 900 million francs to redeem the mineral resources. However, whether Germany can pay within a year remains questionable. Regarding the latter issue, the agreement stipulated that Germany should ensure the safety of those who voted against returning to Germany. However, in reality, the National Socialist Party has special methods of dealing with such individuals. Therefore, whether this provision will be merely symbolic remains uncertain. If these two issues are not properly resolved, the Saar's return to Germany may not be fully realized in the short term. Even if it does return, the specific terms and conditions, both complete and partial, are still subject to the League of Nations Administrative Council's decision. Therefore, it cannot be said that everything is settled after the vote.

Looking at it from the German perspective, according to a Reuter's dispatch yesterday, the German people seemed rather indifferent to the Saar plebiscite. When the authorities ordered people to wear lapel flowers, less than one-tenth complied. Even fewer hung flags to celebrate. Their enthusiasm was far less than that of government officials. This phenomenon seems quite peculiar at first glance, but upon closer inspection, the reason is quite ordinary. According to the treaty, the Saar's return was originally supposed to occur after fifteen years. When Hitler came to power, he directly negotiated with France to return the Saar early, without requiring a plebiscite. This request was rejected by France. Therefore, today's plebiscite is purely the result of the fifteen-year term expiring. There was no acceleration in time, nor any concessions gained in redeeming the mineral resources. Everything was done according to the treaty. Therefore, the Germans view the victory of this Saar plebiscite as a matter of course, with not a trace of luck involved. The reason for the lack of overwhelming enthusiasm may be this. However, according to today's news, when the Germans heard the news of the plebiscite victory, they were overjoyed and shouted with joy, like fathers and sons, brothers reuniting after a long separation, filled with joyful tears, which is also a very normal thing.

Winter Relief in Jiangxi Province Begins 27

(Nanchang) Winter relief, in the form of congee distribution at four locations, began today. Destitute refugees are crowding in. The city's women's community, finding the four congee distribution sites insufficient, will add a women's congee distribution site. (Fifteenth Dispatch)

(Nanchang) International reporter de Prelle cabled the Red Swastika Society's Jiangxi relief group, stating that the banditry and disaster in Jiangxi are unprecedented in the world, and the severity of the disaster calls for aid from everyone. He requested a preliminary investigation so that upon arrival in Jiangxi, he can appeal to all nations for compassion with the findings. (Fifteenth Dispatch)

(Nanchang) The Red Swastika Society has begun accepting people in Hengfeng, with a large influx of sick people seeking treatment. The Provincial Relief Association has accepted 7,000 refugees from Ningdu, Yu, Xingguo, and Xiaojiang in Guangchang, excluding the young and strong. (Fifteenth Dispatch)

Northeast Region

Japanese Forbid Christian Preaching 34

Zhang Ting'e Talks

No Expansion Plans for Tianjin 35

(Tianjin) Zhang Ting'e stated that whether Tianjin will be expanded or reorganized depends on whether the provincial government relocates. The organization of a city where the provincial government is located is naturally that of an ordinary city. Therefore, everything remains as before and no reorganization preparations have been made. Rumors that Tianjin will be developed as a commercial city, expanding its municipal area, are unfounded. The Tianjin Municipal Government has established a health bureau to handle the city's health administration and directly collect health taxes. This is the prelude to establishing a health bureau. The original health office of the Municipal Government still exists but only handles design and construction matters. (Fifteenth Dispatch)

Yu Xuezhong will serve as the chairman, and the Finance Commissioner, Lu Muting, as the deputy. There will be seven committee members, including five from the Provincial Committee and one each from the Party Committee and the Donation and Tax Supervision Committee. In the future, the method of assigning land tax to the province and surcharges to the county will be implemented. Before the land is reported, it will continue to be managed as before. Plebiscite Results Announced: Saar Region Returns to Germany 40

Pro-Return Votes Account for Ninety Percent; Fifteen Years of Lost Territory Recovered in One Day; German People Rejoice and the Whole Country is Ecstatic

The final results of the Saar plebiscite in Saarbrücken were officially announced this morning. The number of votes in favor of returning to Germany exceeded even the expectations of German leaders. The official final vote count is as follows: 477,119 votes in favor of returning to Germany, 46,513 votes in favor of maintaining the status quo, and 2,124 votes in favor of returning to France.

Calculated as a percentage of the total vote:

90.36% in favor of returning to Germany, 8.81% in favor of maintaining the status quo, and 0.40% in favor of returning to France.

Although voters were scattered far and wide, very few Saarlanders with voting rights abstained. The total number of registered voters was 539,541, of whom 528,005 actually voted, with only 11,536 abstaining.

After the official results were announced at the Warteberg Hall, the people of the Saar cast aside all the restrictions imposed during the voting period and celebrated the return of their lost territory to the motherland with a unanimous voice of joy. Tens of thousands of people came out to celebrate, and swastika flags could be seen fluttering everywhere in the freezing wind. Homes were brightly lit with candles, and the bells of churches rang throughout the region. Hundreds of residents along the border rushed into Germany to express their intention to return to their rightful owners. Although the minority was overshadowed by this universal celebration, they were unwilling to remain silent. Saar Social Democratic leader Blum also convened an anti-Hitler demonstration. According to the results of this vote, the rural areas almost unanimously favored returning to Germany, while the industrial areas favored maintaining the status quo. (Fifteenth National Telegraph Dispatch)

The German victory in the Saar plebiscite in Saarbrücken was expected, but the number of votes it received was surprising. It was generally believed that if the number of votes in favor of returning to Germany was less than 85 percent, it would be a blow to Hitlerism. Today's results indicate an undeniable victory for the National Socialist Party. There were many spectators in the Warteberg Hall during the vote counting, but not many people gathered outside because of the cold weather. (Fifteenth Reuters Dispatch)

Hitler's Broadcast Speech 41

Welcoming the Saar's Return to the Motherland; Shame of the Post-War Era Now Eradicated; No More Territorial Demands on France; Church Bells Ring and Swastika Flags Fly; Berlin and the Saar Celebrate Together

German Führer Hitler declared tonight that after the Saar's return to Germany, Germany will no longer have any territorial disputes with France. Hitler also said that people of the same race and culture expressed their judgment with one voice. There is no greater honor for us than this. Today, I represent all German people in expressing our gratitude. Today, I cannot help but say that we will never hinder the unity of all nations, and we are also determined to create equality for all nations. People of the Saar, you can be said to be worthy of being German. Tens of millions of Germans thank you and welcome you back to a unified Germany, and so on. (Fifteenth National Telegraph Dispatch)

(Berlin) All of Germany is celebrating the Saar's great victory today. National flags are flying throughout the city, and all private residences, trams, and automobiles are decorated with flags to celebrate. Workers in factories and employees in businesses gathered in front of radios to listen to the results of the plebiscite. They only started working after learning the results. Schools across the country also broadcast the good news by radio. After hearing the good news, German Führer Hitler issued a radio address, welcoming the people of the Saar back to Germany, saying that the shame of the past few years has now ended. The joy of the Saar's return is the joy of all German people. The people of the Saar have been strong and patient in the past fifteen years, which is commendable. He also hoped that they would continue to maintain discipline in the future. He also said that we are determined to safeguard world peace. Now that the Saar has returned, Germany no longer has any territorial demands on France. Although Germany seeks equality and security, it is also willing to facilitate the unity of all nations. After Hitler's speech, it was followed by a hymn praising God, then the Saar anthem, and finally the ringing of church bells throughout Germany. Churches were ordered by the Minister of the Interior to ring their bells for one hour from noon to 1:00 PM. (Fifteenth Reuters Dispatch)

(Berlin) German Commissioner for Saar Affairs Josef Bürckel gave a speech when the results of the plebiscite were announced, congratulating Führer and Chancellor Hitler, saying that "The Saar people's vote in favor of returning to the motherland by 90.5 percent indicates that the people's desire to end the millennia-long unrest is self-evident. The Rhine River is not the border of Germany, but its inner river. The Saar people's desire to merge with the German motherland and their faith in Germany has been clearly demonstrated. Hitler, you are Germany, you are the protector of the children of the fatherland." After Bürckel's speech, Hitler gave a reply, saying that the injustice of the past fifteen years has now come to an end, and the suffering of our Saar compatriots has also come to an end. Today's joy of the Saar people is also the joy of the German people. Hitler then recounted the injustice of the Treaty of Versailles and praised the courage and loyalty of the Saar people. He then said, "The tension in Europe has now disappeared. The disputes in Europe for the past twenty years have been resolved in one fell swoop. Therefore, January 13th is a memorable day. Since the Saar people have made this decision, I dare to solemnly declare that after the Saar returns to Germany, we will no longer have any territorial demands on France. We want Germany to obtain equality of rights, but we also want to realize the solidarity of all nations." Then, Propaganda Minister Goebbels gave a speech, saying, "Hundreds of thousands of people in the Saar, regardless of gender, class, or occupation, have shown their patriotic fervor, resulting in Germany's victory in the fifteen-year dispute. This is something that we German people should never forget for generations to come." On this day, all German schools and public institutions hung flags to celebrate. The Christian and Catholic authorities ordered all churches to ring their bells for one hour. In addition, the entire nation was asked to hang national flags, so that within half an hour, the entire country was covered in flags. German universities will hold celebrations, and there will be large-scale demonstrations in public places across the country, praising the patriotism and loyalty of the Saar people. (Fifteenth Havas Dispatch)

French Prime Minister's Declaration 42

No Objections to the Voting Results; Dawn of Peace in Europe; Hopes that All Issues Between the Two Countries Can Be Resolved Under the Supervision of the League of Nations

(Paris) In light of the clear voting results, the French government today advocated returning the Saar to Germany immediately, but recognized that the rights of the anti-Hitler minority should still be protected. The French Prime Minister declared this afternoon that the resolution of the Saar issue is a dawn of peace in Europe and greatly contributes to improving Franco-German relations. From now on, the two countries can cooperate for peace in Europe, and so on. (Fifteenth National Telegraph Dispatch)

(Paris) Prime Minister Flandin issued a statement on the results of the Saar plebiscite, stating that "France's international policy is based on adhering to treaties. It is gratifying that the plebiscite held in the Saar region has been conducted strictly in accordance with the treaty. The French people will not raise any objections to the voting results." Prime Minister Flandin then described the League of Nations' contribution to maintaining peace and said that he hoped that all issues that hinder the improvement of relations between France and Germany could be resolved quickly under the leadership of the League of Nations. The issue of relocating Saar residents to other countries is significant and closely related to the League of Nations, as the League of Nations should protect opponents of Hitler to prevent retaliation. Prime Minister Flandin, while deeply confident that the German government will respect the rights of minorities, still stated that the French government has paid attention to this matter and organized an inter-ministerial committee chaired by Minister without Portfolio Herriot to draft a plan. (Fifteenth Havas Dispatch)

British Government Delighted; Clouds Dissipate and Central European Problems Can Be Solved Easily 43

(London) The British government expressed its delight this morning upon learning of the Saar's return to Germany. Powerful sources declared that the announcement of the vote was sufficient to dispel the clouds over Europe and that issues such as concluding a disarmament treaty, signing an Eastern European pact, and Germany's return to the League of Nations could be easily solved. The British government believes that the League of Nations Administrative Council no longer needs to discuss the status quo issue because the number of votes in favor of returning to Germany is so large. (Fifteenth National Telegraph Dispatch)

League of Nations Committee Meeting; Advocates Returning Sovereignty of the Saar Region to Germany; Awaiting Final Decision from Administrative Council Meeting 44

(Geneva) This afternoon, the League of Nations Saar Committee met, chaired by Italian Aloisi, and decided in principle to advocate returning the Saar to Germany. The full text of the resolution will be submitted to the League of Nations Administrative Council tomorrow. Although Germany's victory was expected by most people, the governments of European countries were all surprised by the majority that Germany obtained in the vote. People in League of Nations circles in Geneva were deeply relieved by the voting results because the number of anti-German votes was quite small, and the final obstacle to returning all the territory to Germany was no longer a concern. Initially, some people feared that if the number of votes against Germany was more than expected, the Saar might be divided. Now, they are all relieved. French newspapers have expressed their satisfaction with Germany's large majority in the vote, saying that it can avoid all kinds of terrible entanglements and hoping that the defeated minority will not put up any major resistance to oppose the will of the victorious majority. (Fifteenth Reuters Dispatch)

(Geneva) This morning, the League of Nations Administrative Council held a non-public meeting for a short time and immediately reviewed the results of the Saar plebiscite and decided to convene a three-person committee to meet in the afternoon to draft a report to be submitted on Thursday or Friday. Then, the Administrative Council will announce the transfer of sovereignty over the Saar region. League of Nations officials have adopted a calm attitude toward the voting results and mostly believe that the number of votes obtained by those who supported maintaining the status quo was less than expected. They believe that, objectively speaking, the results of this vote were similar to the plebiscites conducted by the German National Socialist government in the past two years. (Note: After Germany withdrew from the League of Nations in 1933, the National Socialist government held plebiscites on domestic and foreign policy to gauge public opinion. After the death of President Hindenburg last year, another plebiscite was held to gauge public support for Hitler's concurrent position as "Führer.") In short, the Saar people did not forget their motherland, and their vote in favor of returning to Germany was due to patriotic psychological reasons. As for whether the National Socialist government should be praised, it is not a matter of concern. However, although the fate of the Saar region has been decided, there are still several political, economic, and financial issues that need to be resolved by the Administrative Council. Specifically, (1) in reference to the resolution passed by the Administrative Council on December 5 of last year, specify the date of transfer of sovereignty over the Saar. According to this resolution, if the voting results decide to return to Germany, the transition period should be at least one month; (2) specify the expiration date of the terms of office of the plebiscite committee and the Saar Administrative Committee; (3) specify the date of withdrawal of international troops. Most of the decisions that the Administrative Council should take on the above matters will depend on the attitude of the Saar officials and people. As for financial and economic issues, the most important are (1) the French franc circulating in the Saar should be recovered with the mark; (2) the future management system of the Saar mines. Regarding these two aspects, the three-person committee specified the outline of the solution last year, and now it should be completed by the Administrative Council. The three-person committee will hold a meeting in a location in northern Italy in the near future, and these issues should be easily resolved. In addition, there is one more issue, namely, according to the Treaty of Versailles, the Saar region is within a demilitarized zone. The French government has not forgotten this, and the Administrative Council should also pay attention to it. (Fifteenth Havas Dispatch)

Politics and Economics: Hundreds of Matters Awaiting Governance 45

With the Saar plebiscite now concluded, one of the most significant chapters of the post-war era has come to an end. The Saar region's mining area, with the northern part being the most important, was largely destroyed during the European War. The Treaty of Versailles, as compensation to France, designated all mineral resources within the Saar as the property of the French state, without any restrictions. The Saar territory was placed under a special system, administered by an administrative committee organized by the League of Nations. French customs regulations were also implemented in the Saar. The Treaty of Versailles stipulated that fifteen years after the treaty came into effect, the people of the Saar would hold a vote to determine their desired sovereignty, namely (1) maintaining the status quo, (2) merging with France, or (3) returning to Germany. The plebiscite held on the 13th of this month was in implementation of this clause. However, as the Saar's mineral resources were owned by France, the treaty also stipulated how to proceed if the voting result was for the Saar territory to return to Germany: Germany would be required to redeem the mineral resources from the French government at a price. The League of Nations would be responsible for handling the agreements needed for the redemption of mineral resources and the transfer of local administrative power. The League of Nations appointed a three-person committee (chaired by Italian representative Aloisi) last year to prepare for the plebiscite and its associated issues. Regarding the various economic and legal issues arising after the Saar's return to Germany, French and German diplomatic representatives signed an agreement in Rome on December 3 of last year. The members of the three-person committee, chaired by Aloisi, were also present at the signing. This agreement stipulated that Germany should pay a total of 900,000,000 francs to redeem the French state-owned coal mines and three railways built by France. In addition to this, the coal mine concessionaire of Warndt should deliver coal to France. The Warndt mine wells are located within France, but the mineral resources are underground in the Saar territory. Regardless of who the operator is, the mine should deliver a certain amount of coal to France each year within five years after the Saar's return to Germany, not exceeding 2.2 million tons per year, totaling 11 million tons over five years. It is estimated that this coal is worth 45 million francs over five years, which is what the French government should receive in addition to the 900 million francs. The Rome agreement also stipulated the payment method: the German government should redeem French banknotes circulating in the Saar with marks, and most of the payment to France would be made with these redeemed banknotes. If there is any remaining balance after the initial five-year period, France will continue to extract coal from the Warndt mine, and the debt owed by Germany to France will be deducted accordingly. Regarding political issues, the German representative had previously stated to Aloisi, the chairman of the three-person committee, that if the Saar returned to Germany, the Third Reich's various laws regarding religion and race would not be implemented in the Saar region for at least one year. This statement was reiterated by the German representative in Rome. In addition, various measures were stipulated to allow Saar residents who wished to leave the Saar to freely exit with their property. Finally, we can briefly describe the quantity of Saar mineral resources: in 1934, Saar coal production reached 11.3 million tons. In 1913, under German administration, it had produced 13.2 million tons, which then gradually decreased, falling to 9 million tons by 1919. By 1924, it reached 14.032 million tons, which was the highest number. The French mining administration had adopted a method of extracting metallurgical coking coal from Saar coal, which was previously unsuitable for this purpose. This new invention was considered particularly beneficial in a place where the steel industry was especially developed and close to the iron mines of the French Lorraine province. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

League of Nations Radio Broadcasts to the World 46

The results of the Saar plebiscite will be transmitted to Geneva between 6 and 7 AM this morning, and will then be notified to League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol. Saarbrücken is scheduled to announce the voting results by radio broadcast at 7 AM this morning. After Geneva learns of the results, it will broadcast them over long distances to all parts of the world via the League of Nations radio station, with wavelengths of 44.94 meters and 20.62 meters. The League of Nations Council is scheduled to hold a closed-door meeting at 10:30 AM this morning. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

Saar Representatives Go to Geneva 47

Three representatives from the Saarbrücken Saar Provincial Assembly, led by German Frontfighter leader Pirro, rushed to Geneva after the voting results were announced to represent the interests of the Saar people and offer opinions when the League of Nations discusses financial and economic issues. All financial and economic issues of the Saar must be resolved before the Saar is handed over to Germany. (National Telegram, 15th)

Ballot Counting Under Arc Lamps 48

The ballot counting work in Saarbrücken began at 5:10 PM yesterday. British soldiers from the international peacekeeping force guarded the inside and outside of the counting place. No one was allowed to enter without two special certificates and a passport. Before entering, they still had to be inspected. A French journalist was excluded for refusing inspection. In the hall of the counting place, sixty tables were set up, with six vote counters sitting at each table. In front of them was a ballot box. During the counting, the plebiscite commission had to sit under the arc lamps. Journalists sat in the audience seats on both sides and took photos of them. Among the guests were International Peacekeeping Force Commander Major General Brian and his staff. At the beginning of the counting, the chairman of the plebiscite commission, Lord, gave a brief speech to warn the vote counters that their responsibility was heavy, and then declared, "The counting can begin now." The vote counters then opened the ballot boxes in front of them, removed all the green-sealed ballots, and placed them on the tables in an orderly manner. The piles of ballots advocating the return of the territory to Germany piled up higher and higher on one table, while the piles of ballots advocating maintaining the status quo piled up on the table were far fewer than the former, but were also gradually increasing. The Saar people did not seem very concerned about the counting, as only about a hundred people gathered outside the counting place. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

The ballot counting was handled in the Wardburg Building, working overnight. By 5:20 AM, all the ballots had been completely counted. From 1 AM onwards, the Dutch member of the public voting commission issued a declaration by radio, saying that the committee could announce the voting results at the specified time and asked all radio listeners to listen to the radio report at 5 AM (German time). After midnight, the number of visitors to the counting place had decreased, but there were still some people who were working hard, maintaining order with the Swedish, Dutch, and British soldiers at the scene.

Page 10

At dawn, there were several other British soldiers in the next room, all with sleeves rolled up, playing cards together. Some were playing the accordion and singing. Only a few British soldiers could be seen at the scene, carrying ballot boxes and large stacks of stamped ballot papers, delivering them to the vote counters' desks. The foreign representatives sat around the stage, and the atmosphere was extremely harmonious. However, some opponents of the Saar's annexation to Germany, seeing that the counting results were gradually in favor of Germany, could not help but feel uneasy. By dawn, the counting of ballots had been completed, but it still had to be reviewed once. The vote counters looked tired because they had not slept all night. Although it was extremely tense yesterday, it changed to tranquility at this time. Only the British soldiers on guard, because they had taken turns sleeping at night, paid attention to the progress of this major historical event all night without fatigue. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

Anti-National Socialist Factions Admit Defeat 49

The various factions of the anti-National Socialist Party in the Saar have admitted defeat in the plebiscite. However, political circles in Paris claim that the plebiscite was very unfair and was held in the atmosphere of National Socialist terrorism. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

Leftist Police Plotting Treason 50

Before the results were announced this morning in the Saar, there was a sudden alarming rumor: after the commander of the Saar International Police and the local police chief went to the Walterburg barracks, it was rumored that some police officers with communist leanings were plotting a coup. But because the plot was revealed, the two masterminds had fled into France. Those who heard about it were shocked. However, after the police commander stated that his visit to the barracks was purely for the purpose of inspecting the barracks, people's minds were calmed. However, the possibility of disturbance has not completely ceased. In the afternoon, the police began to arrest communists, and 16 people have been arrested. It is reported that some weapons were found in their rooms. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

(Berlin) The official communications agency accused Knox, the chairman of the Saar management committee, of failing to perform his supervisory duties, and accused the management committee of being biased, saying that 120 special police officers plotted to seize power, but the plan was not secret. The commander of the international police, Hanassi, inspected the camp and ordered the confiscation of all weapons. Several masterminds fled elsewhere. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

Saarbrücken Yesterday night, an incident occurred in the police barracks of Saarbrücken City, Saarbrücken. Police officers who advocated maintaining the status quo, fearing that the plebiscite results might be unfavorable, caused disturbances, resulting in a conflict with police officers affiliated with the German Front Group. It was pacified by the intervention of the police chief. At that time, the police in the camp were temporarily disarmed, but the weapons were returned soon after. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

(Berlin) Regarding the conflict that occurred in the Saar district police barracks last night, the German News Agency issued a special publication at 2:15 AM this morning, saying that the Saarbrücken City Police Department learned last night that a German fugitive named Machzi had gathered 120 people to organize a special team aimed at splitting the Saar region into two parts, one part belonging to Germany and the other part maintaining the status quo. The German News Agency used this as an excuse to launch a strong attack on Knox, the chairman of the Saar Administrative Committee, accusing him of deliberately condoning (fugitives) to serve as police officers, causing the incident last night. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

Important British Cabinet Meeting Plans to Invite Germany Back to Geneva 52

Considering the Lifting of Military Clauses in the Treaty, Britain, France, and Italy Will Strive to Find a Way. French Authorities Plan to Visit London at the End of This Month

(London) The British Cabinet held an important meeting last night to discuss the international situation. It is expected that there will be new developments in European political circles. Soon, Britain and other countries will contact Germany, aiming to have Germany rejoin the League of Nations and participate in a disarmament convention. It is believed that the British Cabinet expressed the opinion at the meeting that the current time is very good, and it is advisable to find a way to seek a general European disarmament agreement again. When French Prime Minister Flandin and Foreign Minister Laval come to England at the end of next week to consult with the British Foreign Minister and others, they will review the entire issue. It is expected that Britain, France, and Italy will strive to find a way to mutually agree to abolish the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles that Germany is most dissatisfied with. However, this method must be attached to the following understandings: (1) Germany rejoins the League of Nations, (2) Germany joins an international convention restricting armaments. According to the phenomenon, the French government now has a more hopeful attitude towards security issues. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

(Paris) French Prime Minister Flandin and Foreign Minister Laval are scheduled to travel from Paris to London on the 25th to consult with British government authorities on European peace work. (Nichi-Ren Telegram, 14th)

(London) How to get Germany to rejoin the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference is one of the main issues currently being considered by the British government. However, Britain is deeply willing to act only after obtaining France's close agreement. Therefore, British policy must wait until Foreign Minister Simon and French Foreign Minister Laval exchange views in London before making a final decision. The British Cabinet will hold a Cabinet meeting on Wednesday to learn about the results of the Saar plebiscite. If the Saar does indeed merge with Germany as a result of the plebiscite, Britain advocates immediately raising the issue of Germany rejoining Geneva without delay. Britain believes that Germany's return to Geneva is an element of European appeasement, and it is especially necessary after the signing of the Rome Agreement and the resolution of the Saar issue. Therefore, experts from the British Foreign Office suggested that the victorious countries of the last war return to the League of Nations the various military benefits obtained from the Treaty of Versailles. (According to their meaning, they refer to the abolition of the military clauses in the Treaty of Versailles.) At the same time, the defeated countries are allowed to request the League of Nations to enjoy the benefits of abolishing these clauses, on the condition that the defeated country joins the League of Nations. The British Cabinet is paying close attention to this plan. However, regardless of the method used, if Germany returns to Geneva, Britain believes that negotiations should be held immediately on a convention restricting armaments. If so, the issue of restricting the use of bombers can be raised for re-discussion.

Discussion, and the Locarno Treaty can also be re-interpreted on the issue of sky safety. If the above issues are raised during the talks between Britain and France in London this month, Britain may express its sincerity in cooperating with the continental countries. However, this cooperation is still limited, because Britain cannot only sign new conventions in the continental area, but also reduce the scope of participation in various forms of international sanctions as much as possible. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

Japanese Youth Invent Aircraft Silencer 53

Claiming 90% Success

(Tokyo) Tokyo citizen Haruji Hatogahara has now completed the invention of a device to prevent the sound of aircraft propellers. The army plans to send General Watanabe and Major General Ishii of the Chemical Research Institute to attend the practical test at the Sozawa area in the afternoon of the 18th. It is said that Hatogahara has spent a lot of effort on this silencer since last year. The results of the test with an Apro 120 horsepower show that it can indeed prevent explosion sounds by up to 90%. It is now apparent that the army sound detectors, which were originally designed to listen to aircraft sounds to detect enemy aircraft attacks, have very limited function. This silencer can be said to be a landmark achievement in national defense, and the general public is paying close attention to it. According to Kajihara, the director of Sozawa Aviation Institute: If this machine is successful, sound detectors will be unnecessary, and it can be said to be the world's greatest invention. It is said that 90% success has been achieved so far. If we continue to work hard from now on, we can reach a perfect state, which is what we hope for. (Nichi-Ren Telegram, 15th)

Kirov Assassination: Zinoviev Exiled 54

But Not Expelled from the Party

(Moscow) Since the assassination of Kirov, there has been a major purge here again. Former Communist Party leaders Kamenev and Zinoviev and many other lesser-known figures were exiled today. It is estimated that 15% to 20% of Communist Party members have been expelled from the party. However, although Kamenev and Zinoviev have been exiled, they have not been expelled from the party. According to the authorities, this purge is due to three needs: (1) to eliminate elements with counter-revolutionary tendencies, (2) to re-purge party members who have joined the opposition of Kamenev, Zinoviev, and Trotsky, and (3) to eliminate party members who express indifference to the Kirov assassination. In addition, Kolundo, vice chairman of the People's Committee of the Belarusian Republic and chairman of the Design Committee, was also expelled from the party. Izvestia reported on this matter, saying that an agency had been uncovered there, which was related to a foreign Pan-Faction and secretly preparing for foreign intervention. In addition, it was heard that the public organs of the two cities of Kiev and Kharkov have also become nests of counter-revolutionaries, but they have no influence in the public. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

US Silver Faction Activities 55

(Washington) Today, all parties in the Washington Congress are paying attention to the currency inflation conference convened by Democratic Senator Thomas, the leader of the inflation faction, to be held on Wednesday. It is said that Democratic Congressman Martin, the leader of the House of Representatives silver faction, also intends to draft his silver proposal after hearing the results of the conference. Congressman Fessinger may make slight modifications to the bill he proposed in the last House of Representatives Currency Committee and propose it again. The content of the proposal is that the government manipulates the purchase of silver to maintain the price balance of 1926. Although Treasury Secretary Morgenthau stated today that the government has no intention of changing or abolishing the 1934 Silver Purchase Act, congressional silver faction leaders still said that the Treasury Secretary is not doing enough to purchase silver. Democratic Senator Wheeler told the Associated Press that the Senate Agriculture Committee will have a favorable report on his proposal to re-establish silver as the US dollar standard at a ratio of 16 to 1 with gold. This report can be submitted to the Senate as soon as there are no other political issues. Webster also said that the attitude of the Treasury Department has made them deeply feel the need to establish mandatory legislation on the silver issue, because the Treasury Department does not sympathize with the silver purchase plan. According to silver faction estimates, the Treasury Department still needs to purchase at least 1.1 billion ounces of silver to meet the legal silver reserve requirements. It is difficult for diplomatic circles to know for sure where the United States can purchase such a large amount of silver. Some diplomats expect that the Treasury Department will re-purchase from silver-producing countries when necessary, rather than starting from silver-using countries. Generally speaking, Mexico may be the best market. (National Telegram, 14th)

(Washington) The panic that the Supreme Court's ruling on the gold clause (test case) will be unfavorable to the government is even more serious today. It is learned that the judges have now begun to study the 1929 ruling of the International Court of Justice on the dispute over the gold clause in Brazilian public bonds. The ruling claimed that Brazilian securities must have a gold clause, and the gold component of the currency paid back must be equal to the component at the time of issuance of the securities. The judges probably attach great importance to this ruling, because the many copies in the Library of Congress have been completely collected, and they are not enough to use. There are no other collections across the country, and a telegram has now been sent to Europe to order them. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau said today that the Treasury Department has begun to study the steps to be taken after an unfavorable ruling, but he is unwilling to discuss what the steps are. Speaker of the House of Representatives Bernes predicted that the Supreme Court will rule to abolish the gold clause, because its relationship to the country is too great, and even if the ruling is unfavorable, the legislative side can find ways to remedy it. However, generally expanding the number of judges and increasing the number of judges who sympathize with the New Deal is something that the country cannot agree to. (National Telegram, 14th)

Ceremony Held in Moscow for Exchange of Famous Chinese and Russian Paintings 56

Soviet Russia Donates Eleven Famous Paintings to China. Chinese Painting Donation Made by Xu Beihong

(Moscow) The ceremony for the exchange of famous Chinese and Russian paintings was held at a tea party hosted by the Cultural Communication Association. Participants included staff from the Chinese Embassy and the Russian Ministry of Foreign Affairs, as well as directors of various museums and artists. Soviet Russia donated a total of eleven famous paintings to China, painted by Repin, Surikov, Ashibov, Kuznetsov, Lentulov, Stirling, Koplin, Rylov, Biyalin, Nizhi, Kebiruri, and Liang Guannan. The paintings donated to Soviet Russia by China have been donated to the Russian side by Mr. Xu Beihong. Chinese Chargé d'Affaires Wu Nanru, Vice Chairman of the Cultural Communication Association Apulatin, and Director of the Museum of Modern Art Beck all gave speeches, all saying that this exchange of famous paintings is only the beginning of the cooperation between Chinese and Russian cultures, and decided to send a telegram to Xu Beihong to express their gratitude. (Central News Agency Telegram, 14th)

Lindbergh Kidnapping Case: Model Also Testifies 57

Handwriting Proven Authentic

A model named Alexander from a clothing store in Flemington testified today that the defendant Hauptmann had contacted Dr. Condon before receiving the ransom. The courtroom was extremely crowded during the retrial this morning. The defendant's lawyer, Reilly, found Alexander's testimony quite strange and questioned her in detail.

Handwriting expert Steing said to the prosecutor today that in his opinion, all the documents were written by Hauptmann. During today's trial, the defendant's lawyer proved that the ransom money obtained by Hauptmann was given by his friend Fisch. A man named Ulrich told the court that he lived with Fisch before Fisch returned to Germany and he was sure that Fisch had given the ransom to Hauptmann.

A Reuters telegram from New York said that the prosecutor had reportedly persuaded Hauptmann to confess the accomplices, in which case he could be spared the death penalty. However, the New York Times said that the prosecutor, Williams, had denied this. The authorities have taken special measures to announce the names of the three witnesses who arrived in the United States from Germany today. After they arrive here, the government will send a car to take them to the designated location, and they will not be allowed to go out until they are ordered to testify. It is believed that one of the witnesses is Fisch's sister. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

The Authority of the Young Turks in Japanese Diplomacy towards North China 99

Frequent personnel changes in negotiations, Sakai's real power surpasses everything

Beijing Correspondence: Japan's diplomatic policy toward North China has always aimed at resolving the entire issue. Before reaching its final goal, it uses a flanking approach, advancing step by step. Minor issues are resolved one at a time, but new ones arise, leading to endless complications. It will not let go until its wishes are fulfilled. Since the establishment of the Tanggu Truce, many issues have been resolved. However, one wave subsides only for another to rise, just like the Northern saying, "endless, never done." Recently, several trivial issues have been resolved, some of which have been announced and some of which have not. However, the Japanese negotiators are still diligently traveling back and forth, pressing forward with increased intensity. This is because the ultimate goal has not been reached, so they continue to use flanking tactics to achieve their wishes. The real power in Japanese diplomacy toward North China lies not with the diplomatic personnel, but with the young military officers. The diplomatic personnel are merely nominal or can only talk but not act. This abnormal reality creates discord. Young military officers have strong desires and ambitions, and tend to advocate for rapid progress. They seem to lack patience with the twists and turns of diplomatic personnel, and accusations are inevitable. Diplomatic personnel have advocated the so-called "water bird diplomacy" as a shield, intending to show that the methods adopted may be different, but their spirit is no different from what the young military officers advocate. However, despite advocating this for a long time, it is still difficult to reduce the accusations. Therefore, some people have strongly advocated the "woodpecker diplomacy," the woodpecker pecking at wood, with both feet clinging to the tree, shaking its head and wagging its tail, being inwardly quiet and outwardly active, taking the meaning of having a master within while actively moving forward. It is advocated to adhere to a fixed diplomatic policy and actively advance. Recently, the Japanese side is still in the midst of disputes over this matter. It is difficult to predict what will happen. However, no matter what, Japan's diplomacy toward North China will become increasingly tighter, which has become an undeniable trend.

The most authoritative of the Japanese negotiators stationed in North China is Sakai, the Chief of Staff of the Tianjin North China Garrison Army. Shiba and Iga, who previously ran around and acted arbitrarily, were merely messengers. Shiba has been transferred back to his country for some reason and replaced by Takahashi, who is Sakai's confidant and will undoubtedly obey his orders. There have been recent rumors that Iga will also be transferred back to his country, but there is no news of his successor. Sakai visited Beijing once a month ago regarding a certain issue, stayed for a day or two, and then returned to Tianjin. The negotiations did not yield any results. In short, North China diplomacy is indeed tighter than before. (January 13th)

Tight Business Conditions in Fuzhou 100

But the Minhou Tax Bureau Actually Increases Taxes

Fuzhou Correspondence: The Gregorian New Year has passed, and the Lunar New Year is approaching. The period for settling debts in the Fujian business community still uses the lunar calendar as the standard. This year, after the victory over bandits, it will definitely be more optimistic than last year's political change. According to those familiar with business conditions, the current business has not yet returned to its original state. The four major export commodities of the province, tea, paper, wood, and bamboo shoots, have all suffered losses due to falling prices and stagnation in foreign ports. The amount of money returned for the year-end settlements (i.e., the redemption of goods) is very small. Most of the money houses have not cleared the huge amounts of money owed by the pawnshops (it is estimated that the total amount owed by the pawnshops to the money houses last year was around one million yuan) and are all wary. Unlike last year, there was a flexible solution of rolling over the debt (transferring the loan debt to a promissory note). Therefore, the number of promissory notes issued for the New Year this year is extremely tight. Although many new banks have been established (it is estimated that four new banks have been established this year: Jiaotong, Shiye, Xingtai, and Nongmin), loans cannot be granted without collateral, which is different from the credit loans of money houses. Therefore, financial conditions are still tight this year and are still in a dangerous period. We must wait until the day of the final settlement to celebrate getting through the difficult situation. However, in order to reorganize tax revenues due to the shortfall in tax revenues last year, the Minhou Tax Bureau has specially increased the business tax of all industries by 20% starting this year, based on the original amount. The various trade associations believe that it is extremely difficult to increase the burden in the current business downturn and convened a meeting at the county chamber of commerce on the 11th, deciding to elect representatives to request the Finance Department of the Provincial Government to exempt them from the increase. It is unknown whether they will be approved. As for the city's grain, due to the poor harvests of both the early and late rice last year due to floods and droughts, unscrupulous merchants took advantage of the high rice prices in Shanghai and smuggled exports to seek huge profits, resulting in the price of high-quality rice reaching ten yuan per picul. Recently, because the selling price of rice produced in Luoluo Annam in Hong Kong is still low, most rice merchants have purchased and transported it to Fujian from Hong Kong to make adjustments. The cost of each picul is only about eight yuan. At the same time, a small amount of rice is also transported to the province from Shaowu and Guangze counties in northern Fujian. Therefore, it is hoped that rice prices will not continue to rise by the end of the lunar year. (January 12th)

This Year is Construction Year for Jiangxi Province 101

Urgent Matters Being Implemented Step by Step

Nanchang Communication: After the bandit scourge in Jiangxi Province, most of the territory is in ruins. Rural production has been completely destroyed. If we want to restore vitality and revitalize various aspects in the future, it cannot be achieved without active construction. Therefore, the provincial government has specifically designated this year as the "Construction Year," selecting simple and easy-to-implement tasks that are most urgently needed for rescuing the dying, healing the wounded, and recuperating, and implementing them step by step. The progress and plans for various aspects such as civil affairs, finance, construction, education, and disaster relief are briefly described below:

The goal of civil administration and political work is to follow the four words "Manage, Educate, Nurture, and Protect" as instructed by Chiang Kai-shek, integrating the four into one. The ongoing measures include: (1) Universally and strictly organizing and utilizing the Baojia system; (2) Vigorously implementing the "Qingxiang" (cleansing the countryside) in newly recovered areas, and completing the anti-communist volunteer corps in various bandit areas; (3) Reorganizing the county-level militia and police to strengthen self-defense; (4) Requiring labor in safe areas and implementing labor construction.

Conscription: Starting this year, conscription will be implemented. The first batch of recruits consists of 32 regiments of new soldiers, who all joined the army on New Year's Day. After that, there will be a batch every six months. The previously recruited regiments can all be transformed into compulsory military service. In a few years, all men aged 21 to 40 will be soldiers. Finance: The annual income and expenditure of the province's finances are both over 17 million yuan. Arbitrary levies have been eliminated by more than 4 million yuan. All counties and localities are also vigorously implementing budgets and final accounts. Starting this year, all expenses for local militias, Baojia, etc., will be centrally collected and disbursed to avoid arbitrary levies and waste.

Construction: (1) Highways: The total length of provincial and county roads in the province is over 9,000 li. This year, in addition to using all the business income of the Highway Bureau as expansion funds, it is also planned to complete the road fees in various places and southern Jiangxi to 3 million yuan. (2) Water Conservancy: To be completed in six years, with a planned annual labor conscription of 10 million and an estimated annual cost of materials of about 1 million yuan. The Fuchu River has already started conscripting labor for dredging. (3) Afforestation: Seedlings are cultivated in seven central areas. (4) The Agricultural Institute, which bears the responsibility of revitalizing Jiangxi, is making steady progress in improving agricultural technology and revitalizing the rural economy. (5) The Provincial Rural Cooperative Association and the China Foreign Famine Relief Committee have established more than 3,000 formal and preparatory cooperatives in the past two years. The Executive Yuan previously allocated 340,000 yuan in funds, and the committee later allocated another 500,000 yuan. If promoted effectively in the future, it can serve as the main force for rural revitalization. In addition, the revitalization of the porcelain industry, the centralized control of wolfram ore, the establishment of paper mills, and the Nanchang Hydropower Plant are also being planned and implemented.

Education: The Department of Education has decided on four major goals: (1) Universalize county education (i.e., realize Baojia-linked schools with Baojia as the hub); (2) Promote special education in newly recovered areas; (3) Expand and restore schools in various places that have been suspended due to banditry; (4) Vigorously implement rural education.

Hygiene: Since the establishment of the Provincial Health Department last year, the National Economic Commission has allocated 200,000 yuan to build a provincial hospital, which is scheduled to be completed this year. The establishment of clinics in bandit areas, county-level hospitals in various counties, the eradication of infectious diseases in various places, and the management of public health are still under development.

Disaster Relief: Although the 24th year of the Republic (1935) is the "Construction Year," bandit disasters, droughts, and floods have spread throughout the province, making disaster relief extremely important. The most important tasks in the future are: (1) Sending stranded refugees back to their hometowns; (2) Urgently assisting the various bandit areas that continue to be recovered; (3) Setting up refugee camps as the suppression progresses; (4) Coordinating drought relief; (5) Cooperating with rural associations to carry out agricultural relief and land reclamation in various places; (6) Organizing work relief; (7) Establishing winter relief associations to distribute porridge; (8) Distributing winter clothing, salt, and medicine. (January 13th)

Establishment of the Cultural Relics Committee of the Former Capital 102

First Meeting Held at the Political Reorganization Committee, Appointing Weng Wenhao, Zhu Qiqian, and Others as Members

Beiping Communication: Since the issue of demarcating the boundaries of Hebei-Peiping Province and City was shelved, the so-called plan to expand Peiping City has turned into the reorganization of cultural relics of the former capital. Previously, when Yuan Liang arrived in Beijing to discuss the demarcation of provincial and municipal boundaries, he had various practical agreements with the central government regarding the methods of reorganizing cultural relics. The central government decided at that time that the first priority was the 3.09 million yuan of operating expenses, and the second was to entrust the Political Reorganization Committee with the overall power and assign the municipal government the responsibility of performing the work. Since Yuan Liang returned to Peiping, he has been preparing step by step in accordance with this method and decided to hold the inaugural meeting of the (Cultural Relics Reorganization Committee of the Former Capital) at 10:00 a.m. today (11th) at the Political Reorganization Committee. In addition to the representatives not sent by the Ministry of Education, the ex officio members include Mayor Yuan Liang, Hebei Chairman Yu Xuezhong, Chahar Chairman Song Zheyuan, Internal Affairs Representative Luo Yaoshu, Finance Representative Ding Chungao, Railways Representative Yin Tong, Communications Representative Shen Jianshi, and Antiquities Preservation Committee and Palace Museum Representative Ma Heng. After the inaugural meeting, the first meeting was held in the conference hall on the fourth floor of the Political Reorganization Committee. In addition to the ex officio members, eight invited members with the nature of experts, scholars, and social celebrities were also appointed, including Zhu Qiqian, Weng Wenhao, Zhu Shen, Chen Hanti, Cheng Ke, Zhou Zuomin, Yuan Dunli, and Fang Juehui, etc. Zhou Zuomin, Yuan Dunli, and Fang Juehui had been appointed but were unable to attend. The secretaries were Xia Qingyi, secretary of the Political Reorganization Committee, and six others. Because the huge amount of 3.9 million yuan had been decided for operating expenses, there was no provision for administrative expenses. Therefore, all office matters were kept simple and frugal. Xia Qingyi and other staff members were borrowed from the Political Reorganization Committee and served concurrently without additional pay. At the meeting today, Chairman Huang Fu discussed and resolved three motions: one was the rules of procedure for the meeting, one was the procedures for implementing the reorganization of culture, and one was the establishment of a committee to manage funds, and Huang Fu, Zhou Zuomin, Ding Chungao, Yin Tong, Yuan Liang and other five people were nominated as the custodians. The meeting adjourned at 12:30. Huang hosted a banquet for all the attending members and important officials in the large reception room of the Political Reorganization Committee. After the meal, Xia Qingyi drafted a report to the central government and related parties on the establishment of the committee. From that day on, the official seal was put into use and office work began. (11th)

Chiang Orders Hubei Construction Department to Complete Shiba Highway 103

Connect Traffic on the Borders of Sichuan, Guizhou, and Hubei, with the Entire Line Divided into Fifteen Sections for Construction

Hankou Communication: Chairman Chiang Kai-shek believes that the Shishi-Baokang Highway in western Hubei is related to the traffic on the borders of Sichuan, Guizhou, and Hubei. Currently, with the westward flight of Jiangxi bandits, Sichuan and Guizhou provinces have become the focus of military operations. It is urgent to complete the road to facilitate encirclement and suppression. He specially ordered the Hubei Construction Department to quickly plan and start construction. After receiving the order, the Construction Department immediately sent Chief Engineer Xu, leading a large number of engineering personnel, to take a boat west from Hankou. The entire line has been divided into fifteen sections for construction on a fixed date. The required funds will be drawn from the 6 million yuan of the 24th year construction public bonds. The starting and ending points and distances of each section are as follows: (1) Enlong Section: from Enshi Airport to Longfeng Dam, 27.5 kilometers long; (2) Longlu Section: from Longfeng Dam to Luzhou Dam, 36.5 kilometers long; (3) Lubai Section: from Luzhou Dam to Baiyangping, 25.0 kilometers long; (4) Baiwu Section: from Baiyangping to Wuyang Bridge, 23.5 kilometers long; (5) Wujian Section: from Wuyang Bridge to the South Gate Bridge of Jianshi, 14.5 kilometers long; (6) Jianxia Section: from the South Gate Bridge of Jianshi to Xiaba Guan, 22.0 kilometers long; (7) Xiayang Section: from Xiaba Guan to Yangpo, 8.0 kilometers long; (8) Yangda Section: from Yangpo to Damaotian, 23.0 kilometers long; (9) Dachao Section: from Damaotian to Chaoyangping, 46.0 kilometers long; (10) Chaolong Section: from Chaoyangping to Longtanping, 47.0 kilometers long; (11) Longzhong Section: from Longtanping to Zhong Sanyuanshi, 47.0 kilometers long; (12) Zhonglu Section: from Zhong Sanyuanshi to Lǜcongpo, 17.5 kilometers long; (13) Lucha Section: from Lǜcongpo to Chadianzi, 37.5 kilometers long; (14) Chashui Section: from Chadianzi to Shuitianba, 27.0 kilometers long; (15) Shuiwan Section: from Shuitianba to Wanhu Tuo, 32.0 kilometers long, totaling 454.0 kilometers. The Zhuzhu and Shiyi highways will also be started one after another. (11th)

Rice Shop Robbed Outside Qingpu South Gate 104

Yesterday evening at about 7:00 PM, more than a dozen robbers with guns and weapons suddenly entered the Zhu Hengfeng Rice Shop outside the South Gate of this city. They first threatened to silence everyone, and then opened the accounting room and looted all the silver dollars and cash. When the Public Security Bureau inspectors heard the news and chased after them, the robbers had already fled south with their loot. After inspection, it was estimated that more than 2,000 yuan was robbed.

Suzhou Sets Deadline to Complete Sukun Road 105

The road built by military engineers between Suzhou and Kunshan, although rugged and hastily constructed, is still an existing thoroughfare. The Provincial Construction Department believes that there is a need for a direct thoroughfare between Suzhou and Shanghai. In addition to the section east of Kunshan, which is being discussed by this department and the Shanghai Municipal Government, it has been decided that the Sukun section will be widened to seven meters based on the original military road. All bridges, estimated to be more than 40, must be rebuilt, and the road surface must also be refilled. The estimated cost of labor and materials is only 300,000 yuan. In order to complete it as soon as possible, the department has dispatched Liu Yeqiu and others to Suzhou to prepare for the project, and also dispatched engineer Xu Zhongming and others to Kunshan on the 15th to inspect the route. As soon as the survey is completed and the design is finished, construction must begin. It is also heard that the deadline is four full months, and the work must be completed and open to traffic by the end of May.

All Suzhou Vegetable Vendors Petition to Abolish Vegetable Tax 106

There are seventeen vegetable markets in Suzhou City. Currently, Wei Du is contracted by the county government to collect vegetable tax, paying 300 yuan per month. Wei then dispatches a large number of tax collectors to collect tax from various vegetable vendors, and even street vendors must pay tax, causing all kinds of harassment. The general petty vendors are full of complaints. The other day, Ji Xiaosong, supervisor of the County Chamber of Commerce, visited County Magistrate Wu to ask him to cancel Wei's contract in order to lighten the burden on petty vendors. Yesterday (15th), the vegetable vendors put forward representatives Yuan Jinsheng and 85 others to submit a petition to the county government, claiming that vegetable vendors have small businesses and cannot afford the monthly tax. They requested that the county government consider the hard-earned money of the poor people and exempt them from paying the摊捐 [tan juan, apportioned levies], in order to make a living.

Wujiang Vegetable Boat Detained in Minhang 107

Due to the severe drought this year, the farmers in the Hubin area are extremely distressed. In winter, they mostly rely on transporting vegetables and other goods to Shanghai for sale in order to make a living. These vegetables were transported by the Zhenze Taihu Vegetable Transportation Company in previous years. This year, there are more shipments, and Zhou Maosheng of Damiaogang has initiated a new shipping company, which charges low fees and is developing very well. Unexpectedly, a shift on December 18th was suddenly detained in Minhang. Because the vegetables were left unattended, they are in danger of rotting, and the farmers dare not load them again. It is now heard that the new company has entrusted someone to intercede.

Wuxi Climate Suddenly Cold, Cleared Up Yesterday 108

In recent months, the county has been experiencing continuous rain and warm weather, like a second spring, so plants are also exhibiting abnormal conditions. Vegetables and broad beans are blooming and bearing fruit one after another. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the day before yesterday (14th), a sudden north wind howled, and the climate suddenly turned cold. The thermometer dropped from over 50 degrees to below 35 degrees, suddenly becoming a severe winter scene. However, there was still drizzle. It was not until yesterday (15th) that it cleared up, and it was still severely cold.

Urgent Tax Collection, Property Confiscated for Those Who Resist 109

The Jiangsu Department of Finance believes that the provincial treasury is extremely short of funds, and the outstanding land taxes of various counties are very large. Therefore, it specially dispatched Commissioner Huang Shi to Wuxi to clear up and strictly pursue the taxes, as urgent as a starfire. Recently, Commissioner Huang and the county government of this county have jointly formulated measures to clear up the old taxes. It is stipulated that each collection office should check the records every day according to the registration of each map section. All those who owe more than one yuan should be extracted household by household, and then extracted in order down to one dime. The list of extractions extracted each day must be made in duplicate, one copy to be handed over to the tax collector for collection, and one copy to be posted on the notice board and issued to the picture chiefs for actual posting of the notice. If the tax is not paid within one month, the property will be confiscated for offset, and the district chiefs and village heads will effectively assist in publicizing.

Jiangyin Property Office Borrows Money to Overcome Difficulties 110

Director Chen Zhongda of the Local Property Office, in order to deal with the arrears of expenses for various agencies and the inability of various creditors to cope with the imminent abolition of the lunar calendar at the end of the year, and because Public Security Bureau Chief Liu Hanzhen was ordered to be transferred to the province a few days ago, and the various chiefs and policemen of the Public Security Bureau were questioning the arrears of expenses for May and June during his tenure, Chen specially submitted a report to the county government on the 12th, requesting the Finance Department to check and indicate that the county taxes from the 17th to the 20th year of the Republic (1928-1931) would be used as collateral, and to temporarily borrow more than 15,000 yuan from the Farmers Bank to overcome the difficulties.

Department Commissioner Urges Collection of Cotton Tax 111

Wu Xiaxia, director of the Jiangjing Business Tax Bureau, has delayed paying the cotton tax. The Finance Department specially dispatched investigator Bao Pugu to Cheng (Jiangyin) and stayed at the China Merchants Hotel to step up the collection.

Jiading Teacher Arrested on Suspicion 112

Tan Songtian, the sixth-grade teacher of the Kuishan Central Primary School in the city, was hired by the Shanghai Guohua Bank for a position and asked Mao Zhongqiu to substitute for him. Mao, 24 years old, claimed to be from Haimen and graduated from Shanghai China Public School. At 6:00 p.m. on the 14th, two people in long clothes, claiming to be members of the Chongming County Party Department, along with many policemen dispatched by the County Public Security Bureau, went to the school to arrest Tan and took away his books and letters. According to the County Public Security Bureau, the teacher is suspected of political activities in Chongming and was arrested by order of the province. He is currently under investigation.

Changshu Clothing Industry Allowed Exemption from House Tax 113

At the beginning of December last year, the Miscellaneous Tax Office of this county suddenly included the clothing industry in the category of shops and increased the collection of house tax. The workers in the industry, because of the high cost of rice and firewood in recent times, could not afford the burden, and repeatedly held meetings in the past month to petition the county government to demand the withdrawal of the tax increase order. It is now learned that County Magistrate Zhai, after consideration, in order to reduce the burden on workers, decided to exempt them from the tax. Yesterday (14th), he formally instructed the trade union that the tax was allowed to be deferred for this year.

Changzhou Xiaohe Sailing Boat Suddenly Robbed 114

The sailing boat from Wuyi City to Xiaohe Town, owned by Shen Hongfu, has recently been ordered to prohibit night travel. Each time the boat sails, it anchors at the Huangniwan Station of the Benniu Railway for the night. Unexpectedly, at about 5:00 a.m. the day before yesterday, when the boat was sailing from Huangniwan to Xiaohe, six robbers suddenly rushed up, armed with guns and weapons, and looted all the silver dollars and other items on the boat. The boat owner reported the case to the Public Security Bureau on the 14th, requesting that the thieves be strictly arrested and brought to justice.

Zhenjiang Merges and Reorganizes Extension Offices 115

In order to save public funds, the Jiangsu Construction Department has ordered that all agricultural extension offices in the silkworm area, except for those that have been merged into provincial demonstration farms, be merged into the silkworm improvement institutes of their respective counties. All extension work will be taken over and continued by the improvement institutes. It is now found that, in addition to Wu County and Jiangdu being merged into provincial demonstration farms, the Jiangsu, Liyang, Jiangyin, Jintan, and Wujin counties have been ordered by the Department to carry out the handover.

Yangzhou Huai River Guiding Association Continues to Urge Recruitment of Laborers 116

The Huai River Guiding into the Sea Engineering Office, because the number of laborers arriving from this county is still insufficient, specially ordered the county government yesterday to continue recruiting as soon as possible to meet the needs of the project. Surveying and Dredging Rivers in the Eighth and Ninth Districts 117

Shu Guohua, Director of the Construction Bureau of Jiangdu County, believes that the work relief in the eighth and ninth districts of this county has been prepared for a long time, and specially dispatched technician Mi Jiyuan to survey the eighth and ninth districts in order. The planned plan is to dredge seven rivers in the two districts, including Tanjiaying and Liangwangzhuang, and to re-dig and control more than forty new and old ponds, so as to compile a budget of the required surveying fees and the price of water and earthworks, and submit the detailed drawings to the county and then to the department for review. It is heard that the relief fund for this project is fixed at 30,000 yuan. Because there are no obstacles in terms of economy, there seem to be no problems in terms of engineering. Qingjiang County Government Executes Murderous Bandit 118

The Huaiyin County Government yesterday received an order from the First Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court to execute the bandit Liu Hengye, also known as Liu Kuishan, who was transferred from Lianshui for robbing and shooting the Xue Shao Xiang couple. After summoning witnesses and confirming that the testimony was correct, a telegram was submitted to the provincial government for approval to carry out the death penalty and to report it accordingly. After receiving the order, the county government extracted the bandit Liu Hengye, also known as Liu Kuishan, on the 12th, verified his identity, tied him to the execution ground, and carried out the execution by shooting. Liu Shutang, the chief of the Second Branch of the local Public Security Bureau, was ordered to go and supervise in order to show prudence.

Puhui Congee Factory Distributes Congee 119

The Huaiyin Puhui Congee Factory distributes thin congee every year as usual to help the starving refugees from near and far. The manager of the factory, Ni Jiafu, has once again raised 10,000 yuan from various places this year, and the Jiangsu Provincial Government has subsidized 6,000 yuan, totaling more than 1,000 dan of rice purchased in the Gaoyou Shiying area. On the morning of the 9th, the rice was officially steamed and distributed. It is estimated that there were no fewer than 5,000 refugees who ate on this day, including local and foreign refugees. The amount of rice required was 20 dan, for a total of 24 pots. Compared with the past when the most congee was cooked, it was still less than four or five pots. However, this is only the beginning of the distribution, and all the refugees who eat from far away have not yet arrived. However, according to the average distribution of the prepared rice, it is only enough for more than a month. Therefore, Ni will continue to go to Beijing and Shanghai to raise funds in order to extend the period.

Jingjiang Opium Paste Company To Be Established Soon 120

The local Opium Paste Company has been vacant until now because no one is willing to undertake it. The opium required by smokers is designated by the provincial government to be purchased from Jiangyin County. Huang Bingyi, of 186 Huage Street, French Concession, Shanghai, believes that the total number of local smokers is more than 1,500, and the daily consumption is very large. Purchasing from Jiangyin is a long way away, separated by the Yangtze River, and the round trip is costly. Therefore, he raised 10,000 yuan and submitted a report to the Anti-Smoking Association, requesting permission to open an Opium Paste Company in the city. The association forwarded the report to the provincial government for review, and the provincial government has now approved the request.

Funing Security Team Kills Two Bandits 121

Two major bandits, Yin Jincai and Li Tingdao, from the Kongsi area in the fifth district of this county, brought box guns to the house of Cai Pingsheng in Caizhuang yesterday to demand 200 yuan in silver dollars, threatening to burn and kill if they refused. Pingsheng pretended to agree to raise the money and secretly informed the second squad of the security team stationed in Banhuzhen. After receiving the report, the squad immediately went to arrest them. Unexpectedly, the bandits heard that the soldiers were coming and immediately opened fire to resist arrest. The police squad returned fire and killed the major bandit Li Tingdao on the spot. Yin was seriously injured. The squad then used a cart to push the wounded bandit back. He died tonight due to his serious injuries.

In the northern village of the county, there have been frequent robbery cases since winter. They broke into the house and tied up each member of the family with hemp rope.

They wantonly looted, taking away a total of about 100 yuan worth of cash, jewelry, and clothes, as well as several dou of white rice. The thieves loaded their stolen goods onto a boat and fled to the southeast. The local Public Security Branch heard the news and dispatched a patrol officer and other police officers to conduct an on-site investigation. A report was submitted to the County Public Security Bureau to strictly arrest the escaped bandits.

In the case of Mark Ogden, Deputy Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council and Chairman of the British American Tobacco Company, being robbed of 83 yuan in paper money by bandits at Zhouliyan, the border between Haining and Haiyan on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway, after receiving a report from Ogden, the provincial government, in addition to ordering the military and police to pursue the bandits, also sent a telegram to the magistrates of Haining and Haiyan counties to investigate the case and report. At the same time, Inspector Ma of the Provincial Public Security Bureau was dispatched with several policemen to escort Ogden back to Shanghai. He arrived safely in Shanghai yesterday and sent a letter to the provincial government to express his gratitude, and explained that the incident occurred 76 kilometers from Hangzhou.

Chen Baozhao, a well-known bandit leader in Yongkang, has committed many cases of murder, arson, kidnapping, and extortion. The provincial government has issued a strict arrest warrant. He was captured by the Yongkang County Security Regiment’s core team yesterday (14th). Suspect in Shi Case Expected to Be Released on Bail 125

Two months have passed since the assassination of Mr. Shi Liangcai, manager of this newspaper, on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway, and there are still no significant clues. Tang Yunsheng, a suspect arrested in Yiwu, has been interrogated several times and found to be unrelated to the case. Xiaoshan's Land Tax This Year is Unlikely to Improve 126

Because the collection of grain tax in Xiaoshan County this year is very light, the superiors have been urging payment urgently. The county government has been sending personnel to the countryside to urge collection for days, but the local area is poor and the number of collections has not improved. In addition, the farmers are only willing to pay 30% of the rent, and even do not return a single grain. Landlords are unable to collect rent and do not pay grain tax, which has a significant impact on national tax revenue.
