Chairman Chiang Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday by Plane 127

Met with Yang Dezhao and Others, Visited Madam Song's Tomb, and Drove Around the City Center; Going to Nanjing This Morning

Financial Stability in Shanghai 133

Both the Silver and Money Trades Can Safely Weather the Year-End

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee, in order to prevent a tight money situation in Shanghai at the time of the final year-end settlement, entrusted the Central Bank to purchase 20 million yuan of silver from Hong Kong for shipment to Shanghai. The first batch has already arrived, and the second batch will arrive soon. However, due to the situation in the Hong Kong market, it is feared that the 20 million yuan cannot be shipped as scheduled before the final settlement. But they have tried their best to arrange for shipment to Shanghai, the more the better.

Financial Stability 134

Shanghai's finances were previously tight due to the autumn harvest in the mainland countryside and the export of silver. The Shanghai money market's overnight loan interest rate reached a peak of sixty cents per thousand. Since the silver and money trades have made every effort to adjust, and the Central, China, and Communications Banks have designated loans and discounts, and after the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee purchased silver and shipped it to Shanghai, it has become stable. The Shanghai money market's overnight loan interest rate has fallen to twenty cents per thousand yesterday, returning to normal, and is even lower than before the annual settlement. As for the loans and discounts made by the three banks, most have already been repaid.

Safely Weathering the Year-End 135

A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency learned from the Silver and Money Trades Association yesterday that in this time of rural decline and business depression, the silver and money trades are taking all lending matters very seriously. Banks only make loans with collateral, and money shops also focus on collateral loans. They are very cautious about credit loans. Therefore, it is predicted that the member banks and money shops of the two trade associations will be able to safely weather the final settlement period of the 23rd year.

Ministry of Finance Stipulates Procedures for Obtaining Permits to Transport Silver 136

Requesting the Ministry of Railways to Instruct Railway Bureaus to Comply

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, the Two Roads Administration received Instruction No. 21 from the Ministry of Railways, which stated: "With the approval of Document No. 11196, Qian Zi, dated December 26 of last year from the Ministry of Finance, it has been in practice for many years to require that a permit be obtained from this Ministry for the transport of silver. Recently, in order to prevent the transfer and smuggling of silver, we have ordered all customs offices to release silver only upon presentation of a permit and not to allow private transport without a permit. However, it is found that silver standard currency should still be freely circulated within the country. Now, at the time of the entry of local products into the market, transportation should be facilitated. The procedures for obtaining a permit are now stipulated as follows:"

Five Procedures 137

(1) When silver and money businesses and ordinary businesses in the capital and Shanghai areas apply for a permit to transport silver, they should still apply to this Ministry. However, banks must attach a guarantee from the Bankers Association, and money shops must attach a guarantee from the Money Traders Association. Businesses must attach a guarantee from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Foreign banks should apply through the Central Bank. (2) In areas outside the capital and Shanghai, customs supervisors are allowed to pre-receive blank silver transport permits from the Ministry and issue them locally. The destination and amount of silver transported should be listed and reported to the Ministry for verification on a monthly basis. The original permits should be returned to the Ministry for verification and cancellation after use. All permit fees and stamp duties should be handled in accordance with regulations. (3) When silver and money businesses and ordinary businesses apply for a permit to transport silver from the nearest customs supervisor, they must have a guarantee from the local Chamber of Commerce or Silver and Money Trades Association. The customs supervisor should verify the information and issue the permit. If there is any collusion to smuggle goods under the guise of this permit, once verified, the supervisor will be removed and punished, and the permit-issuing businesses and guarantors will be dealt with in accordance with the smuggling penalty measures. (4) In areas without customs offices, if the amount of silver coins transported is more than one thousand yuan, a certificate should be issued by the local Chamber of Commerce or Silver and Money Trades Association for presentation to checkpoints and military police along the way for inspection. (5) All guarantees should ensure that the transport is for legitimate domestic commercial purposes and that there is no transfer or smuggling. Violators will be held jointly responsible. The certificate should certify the amount, destination, and actual purpose of the transport and that there is no transfer or smuggling. Violators will be held jointly responsible.

Trial Implementation Today 138

The above five items have been modified to some extent based on current practices, so that laws, regulations, business conditions, and overall considerations are taken into account. They will be implemented on a trial basis starting today. If the amount of silver transported is more than one thousand yuan and the transporter does not have a permit from this Ministry or a certificate from the local Chamber of Commerce or Silver and Money Trades Association, the silver should be detained and referred to this Ministry for processing. In addition to separate consultations, the Ministry requests your department to investigate and instruct all road bureaus to comply, and to further instruct all stations to comply. This order has been forwarded by the Road Bureau to the Transportation Department for compliance.

Note: The execution of the fourth item has been temporarily suspended, as seen in the Ministry of Finance's order of the tenth day.

Xu Shiying Returned to Shanghai Yesterday, Talking About Receiving 300,000 in Relief Funds 139

Another 250,000 Will Also Be Allocated Soon, and the Rural Loan Group Has Already Begun Organizing

Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Relief Committee, went to Beijing on official business a few days ago. He completed his work the day before yesterday and returned to Shanghai by river steamer, arriving at the port at about 2 p.m. yesterday. He returned to his residence to rest, and at about 4 p.m., he went to the Famine Relief Association for Various Provinces to review official documents. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Xu at the Association, who spoke about the situation of his trip to Beijing to negotiate various important matters as follows:

300,000 in Relief Funds Remitted to Shanghai 140

Mr. Xu first stated, "The greatest task of my trip to Beijing was that the weather is now becoming increasingly cold, and the general disaster victims are suffering from both cold and hunger. The matter of providing relief is urgent and cannot be delayed. Therefore, when I went to Beijing, I had a thorough discussion with the authorities, and they immediately allocated 300,000 in cash, which was remitted to Shanghai. Our association has now received the funds and will immediately send personnel to various disaster areas to provide relief. Another 250,000 will also be allocated as soon as our association prepares the official procedures and submits them to the government. The timeframe should be no more than ten days. As for the association's plan to hire a Western consultant, because there is no need in fact, and it would only increase expenses, it has been temporarily postponed."

Revitalizing the Countryside by Forming a Loan Group 141

Mr. Xu further told the Central News Agency reporter, "I (Mr. Xu referring to himself) went to Beijing this time because I felt that the bankruptcy of the countryside was becoming more and more acute, and it was necessary to provide relief as soon as possible. Therefore, I suggested to the government that a rural loan group be established. It is known to all that 85% of our country's population are farmers, and China is founded on agriculture. If we sit idly by and watch the bankruptcy of the countryside, how can the economy of the entire country and society be maintained? Although the financial authorities have stipulated that the banking sector should do its best to invest in the countryside, Shanghai is the financial center of the country, and most banks still neglect to invest in the countryside. Now, although the banking sector can pay attention to this, the results of my consultations with the authorities in Beijing this time are to jointly organize a rural loan group with the major banks in Shanghai. The capital is tentatively set at 10 million yuan, with the Central Bank responsible for 30% of the total, and the remaining 70% to be invested in the countryside by the major banks according to the size of their capital. After the capital is collected, a rural loan group will be organized. The group's operations will be planned by those with specialized knowledge of rural finance, and those with rich experience and knowledge of rural finance will be invited to serve as the head of the group. I will convene the heads of the major banks in Shanghai in the shortest possible time to discuss and implement active measures. I firmly believe that the rural economy can be revitalized in this way, which is the fundamental way to restore the national and social economy. Otherwise, if the 85% of farmers are in a state of deep distress and are not given effective relief, the remaining 15% of the people will also find it difficult to stabilize their lives."

Huangshan Construction to Be Carried Out in Stages 142

Mr. Xu concluded, "Regarding the Huangshan construction project, I convened the committee members in Beijing this time to earnestly discuss the implementation plan. It was decided to carry it out in three years. This year is designated as the transportation construction year, next year as the production construction year, and the year after as the cultural construction year. Five years later, the Huangshan Administration Bureau will be established, and all local affairs will be the responsibility of the Bureau to promote, as a model for national autonomy. The committee is now proceeding diligently according to the established principles to see it through to completion."

The Last Person to Vote in Saar Was a German Woman Living in Shanghai 147

Mrs. Mengtena Chu Rushed 8,000 Miles to Fulfill Her Civic Duty

In matters concerning the public, it is important for those involved to unite and bravely fulfill their responsibilities in order to succeed. Conversely, if there are difficulties and everyone shirks responsibility, there is no way to avoid failure. In this Saar plebiscite to determine the region's allegiance, judging from the general trend, the majority of the 540,000 votes will favor returning the land to Germany. Therefore, the German victory is certain. However, the Germans still do not rely on their certainty of victory and slack off. Those who were born in the Saar but live overseas do not mind the hardship of travel, trek long distances, and return to their homeland to fulfill their responsibilities. There are indeed many. Some returned from South America, some traveled far from Japan, and one German woman from Shanghai also rushed and traveled quickly for this matter, finally reaching her destination on the day of the vote and being the last person to vote. This spirit of unity and bravery in fulfilling one's responsibilities is worthy of our admiration and emulation. It is specially recorded as follows: After Germany's defeat in the European War, it suffered the humiliation of being forced to sign the Treaty of Versailles, which was heavily binding. Even today, Britain is proposing to abolish the military provisions of the treaty and treat Germany as an equal (see today's Reuters report). This is not without this spirit leading to it.

Three months ago, Mrs. Mengtena Chu, a German woman, heard that the Saar plebiscite was scheduled.

The Money Trade Announces February 3rd as the Final Settlement Date for the 23rd Year 148

The time for collecting bills is extended, and interest is set to stop for four days starting on the 4th to sort everything out.

The Shanghai Money Trade Association decided to set February 3rd as the final settlement date for the 23rd year. Yesterday, it notified all member money shops to comply. The notification is recorded below: "To whom it may concern, with regard to the proposal of the 15th meeting of the 2nd membership representative conference, the handling of business before and after the final settlement of the 23rd year was discussed and resolved. February 3rd of the 24th year was set as the final settlement date for the 23rd year. From February 4th to the 7th, there will be a four-day holiday after the final settlement to sort everything out. This four-day period will be the dismissal period. The remaining three items, such as the interest issue before the final settlement, the bill collection period, and the overnight loan interest rate, will be fully decided by the standing committee entrusted by the representative conference. They are recorded in the minutes. At the 67th meeting of the 2nd standing committee on the 12th of this month, the following was resolved: (1) Regarding the interest issue before the final settlement, it was decided that from January 1st to the 15th, the deposit interest rate will be 11.95 yuan, and the overdue interest will be added as usual. The deposit interest rate from the 16th will be decided by the executive committee on the 25th and announced later. (2) Regarding the bill collection period, it was decided that it will be until 4 p.m. on January 29th. The return of bills will be extended by one hour as usual, and they will be settled as soon as they arrive on February 3rd. (3) Regarding the overnight loan interest rate, it was decided that the market overnight loan interest rate will be open until February 2nd. The above resolutions have been recorded in the minutes. This notification is hereby issued, and it is hoped that you will check and comply."

As the vote drew near, she went to the German Consulate General in Shanghai to apply for permission to return to the Saar to vote. After a long time, she did not receive a reply, and at first thought that she had lost her opportunity to fulfill her responsibilities. But on Christmas Day, she suddenly received a phone call from the consulate, saying that according to a telegram from the government, the matter could be carried out as requested, and asked if she could go to the consulate the next day to discuss it. Mrs. Chu was overjoyed to hear the news, and without waiting, she went to the consulate the next day and learned that the consulate not only approved her return home to vote, but also offered to buy her a boat ticket. This was on Wednesday, December 26th. The next day, Thursday, Mrs. Chu was busy all day, without taking a break, because her passport still needed to be signed by the Soviet and Polish consulates. On Friday, Mrs. Chu packed her luggage, and her husband withdrew travel and living expenses. At 9 a.m. on Saturday morning, she boarded a Japanese ship to Dalian, and then rushed to Harbin from that port. However, the Siberian rain and snow blocked the way for the train, and Mrs. Chu was extremely anxious, fearing that she would arrive in Saarbrücken after the voting period. When German Aviation Minister Göring heard that Mrs. Chu had returned from afar to fulfill her responsibilities, he worried that she would be late and disappointed, so he specially prepared a plane for Mrs. Chu to ride in. On one hand, he asked the Saar Committee to specially allow the plane to fly over the border. According to a Saarbrücken telegram from the National Society on the 13th (today, the last person to vote here was Mrs. Mengtena Chu. Because she rushed to vote, she traveled from Shanghai, taking a ship, train, and plane along the way, covering a total of 8,000 miles, so she was very tired when she arrived here. When she took a car to the polling station to vote, her face was filled with joy, as if to show that she had fulfilled her responsibilities). According to the report, Mrs. Chu first arrived in Shanghai from Germany and worked as a watch tester at the China Clock Company. In 1926, she married Mengtena Chu. Mr. Meng has a shop at No. 1163 Jing'an Temple Road. Mrs. Chu has a mother who is 77 years old and seven brothers and sisters, all living in Saarbrücken. According to her husband yesterday, Mrs. Chu will stay for a few months to enjoy the joy of family.

Howard Speaks on India's New Constitution 149

National News Agency, 本埠消息, The British Universities Association held a luncheon at the Kyoto Hotel yesterday afternoon, chaired by President Kim, and invited Howard, chief writer of the North China Daily News, to speak on India's new constitution. President Kim first thanked the Chinese members on behalf of the British members of the association for their hospitality at the International Sports Association last month. Then, he introduced Mr. Howard, saying that he had lived in India for many years, first as a journalist, then as a British official, and participated in the Simon Commission. Howard stood up and said that India's new constitution was neither a prelude to independence from Britain nor a conspiracy to squeeze out Gandhi. In fact, it was only the inevitable result of Britain's policy towards India since 1833. According to the British Parliament's Act of 1833, the East India Company was abolished, and the relationship between the Indian people and their government was also established. When the British House of Commons discussed the Indian Act, Lord Macaulay paid special attention to the future of the Indian Empire, because at that time he had foreseen that as a result of Europeanization, the Indians would inevitably demand a Western political system. A hundred years ago, this Scotsman foresaw today's new constitution for India by the British government, which is truly amazing. The secret behind the growth of Indian nationalism can be found in Panipat. Panipat is a small village between Delhi and Ambala. Three times, the fate of India was decided in this small village. Each battle was won by the invaders. The last battle took place in 1761, four years after the Battle of Plassey. Those who read British history know it well. As a result of this battle, the British power to rule India was established, and India no longer feared invasion, and the Indians became accustomed to living in peace, and nationalism grew and developed under British guidance. Nationalism is also the precursor to parliamentary government. The policy of allowing Indians to participate in politics only dealt with Indian representation until the Morley-Minto Reforms. Since the declaration of 1917 and the establishment of the current temporary constitution, the responsibility system has been partially introduced into the political system, and this responsibility system has a distinction of division. The so-called division is to retain certain powers of the government, and transfer the remaining powers to the Indian officials who are responsible to the provincial council. This system was set to be reviewed after ten years. Therefore, the Simon Investigation Committee was established. The chairman of the committee is the current Foreign Secretary Simon, and Edward Cadogan, the brother of the Minister to China Cadogan, is also a member. Edward Cadogan is the person who signed the Simon Report. The Simon Report advocated provincial autonomy in India, but with the establishment of an All-India Federation as the ultimate goal. The members of the committee believed that the past constitutional acts were specifically established for British India, and there would be no long-term solution if the various states of India were not considered together. Therefore, they advocated that such a plan could be implemented on a trial basis when the Indian princes volunteered to participate in the federation. Something unexpected happened. When the round table conference was first held, the Indian princes expressed their willingness to participate in the federation. This completely changed the situation, and the Indian constitutional reform plan had to stipulate the All-India Federal Political System in addition to stipulating provincial autonomy. There is only one prerequisite, that is, more than half of the Indian princes must participate. The Indian Federation has become a unique entity, with one part of its composition being the provinces of British India under civil rule and the other part being the Indian states ruled by princes. The risk of implementing such a constitution is great, but the risk of not doing it is also great. If the risk is not taken, the achievements that Britain has made in India in the past cannot be obtained. Any constitution has safeguards. The word safeguard causes misunderstanding, but its intention is to allow responsible government to be implemented. Without this safeguard, the entire plan may fail. India cannot have an organized and sound political party in Britain, and strong public opinion sufficient to cope with administrative problems. India cannot allow its two major groups of different religions and cultures to participate in politics side by side. Therefore, constituency elections are indispensable. Some people think this is an obstacle to responsible government, but the Simon Committee does not think so. It is already very difficult to transfer the responsibility for law and order in each province to the Indian officials. If it is not so, the so-called provincial autonomy is equal to empty talk. Moreover, the Indians have shown that they can take responsibility for law and order. Therefore, the Simon Committee's suggestion has been adopted by all parties. The so-called safeguards are that diplomacy and defense are still retained by the Governor-General of India and are not within the jurisdiction of the Federal Parliament. Regarding India's defense issues, this is indeed indispensable. There is also an important provision in the constitution, that is, the Indian railways are generally under the jurisdiction of a special railway authority to avoid interference from political forces, because the Indian railways are all state-owned, and they are very important to the national interests. The existing railways are a total of 79,000 miles long.

Page 13

Hapag and Norddeutscher Lloyd Express Liners

Scheduled Sailings Connecting the Atlantic 150

Hapag Sails on April 16, Norddeutscher Lloyd Sails on June 25

Messrs. Melchers & Co., managers of Norddeutscher Lloyd and Hapag lines, are building high-speed new vessels to compete in the Europe-Asia trade, adding special express services to Central Europe. Norddeutscher Lloyd and Hapag are each adding two vessels. This matter was previously noted in this newspaper. Now, the first new vessel of Hapag is expected to arrive in China within five weeks on its maiden voyage. The first new vessel of Norddeutscher Lloyd is also expected to depart from Germany on May 8. It is expected that the Central Europe route will cause a great surge in express services. This matter is closely related to the Central Europe trade, and it is urgent to investigate and record it as follows.

Hapag's Central Europe Express Mail Steamer Cordillera

Hapag's New Vessel Expected to Arrive in Hong Kong 151

Hapag and Norddeutscher Lloyd stand on the same front in the Far East trade, so this year they have increased the number of Central Europe express vessels, with each side opening two vessels. The first vessel of Hapag is the newly built mail steamer Cordillera. The Cordillera is 525 feet long, 65 feet wide, and 41 feet high, with a displacement of 16,000 tons. It uses an eight-cylinder diesel engine with 11,000 horsepower and travels at 17 nautical miles per hour. The first-class cabin has 149 rooms, the second-class cabin has 100 rooms, and the third-class cabin has 110 seats. All cabins are outside the deck corridor and are not subject to the heat of the engine room. All first, second, and third-class cabins have tea dance halls, grand halls, smoking rooms, library rooms, gyms, soda fountains, merchandise stores, barbershops, swimming pools, and so on. The glass hall can be opened and closed, and it can be called the world's most modern ship. The first voyage is scheduled to depart from Germany on February 20 and arrive in Shanghai on April 2.

Norddeutscher Lloyd's New Vessel Rushing to Install Cabins 152

Norddeutscher Lloyd's new Far East express vessel, the first vessel Scharnhorst, was launched on the 13th of last month and is now being processed to rush to install cabins. The vessel has a displacement of 17,000 tons and is 615 feet long. The cabins are divided into first and second class. The interior layout is based on the style of the Atlantic first-class giant mail steamers. Its luxury and grandeur are beyond the current Central European vessels. The swimming pool is located on the upper deck and is accessible to sunlight. Colored silk umbrellas are hung on the deck, and there are wine bars, soda fountains, and sports fields, so that passengers can rest after swimming, just like on the beach. Its various advantages are too numerous to mention. The speed is even stronger, and it can travel at 19 nautical miles per hour. It is limited to being completed by the end of April. The second vessel, Gneisenau, is the same size as its sister ship and is expected to arrive in Shanghai five months later.

Maiden Voyages of Two Fast Steamers 153

The Hexpol Cardillera has been scheduled to depart next month, stopping at twelve ports en route to Shanghai, and also calling at Yokohama and Kobe in Japan. Therefore, its first maiden voyage to Shanghai has been set for April 16th, heading to Naples, Italy. As for the North German Lloyd's Xianghuosituo, it is expected to arrive in Shanghai from Germany on May 8th, stopping at fifteen ports along the way. Its first voyage will traverse various Mediterranean countries, so it is estimated to arrive in Shanghai around June 13th, also calling at Japan. The maiden voyage from Shanghai to Europe has been set for June 25th. The Hexpol's second ship, the Ribosidun, is larger than the Cardillera and has stronger horsepower. It only offers first and second class cabins, with greater luxury than the first ship. The departure date has not yet been determined. The North German Lloyd's second ship, the Rina Aesino, Gneisenan, has 152 first-class cabins and 142 second-class cabins and is expected to arrive in China at the end of the year.

Atlantic Route Can Be Connected 154

The Hexpol and North German Lloyd's express steamer routes not only shorten the voyage from Shanghai to Europe, but also connect to the Atlantic, linking with major European and American ships. The Hexpol Cardillera's route is from Shanghai to Naples, Italy, then to Marseille, via Barcelona, Spain, and then to Southampton, a major Atlantic postal hub. The North German Lloyd's Xianghuosituo and other two ships also go to Naples from Shanghai, via Hong Kong, Little Luzon, Singapore, Piraeus, Belawan Colombo, and Posey. It only takes 23 days to reach Italy, one day faster than the current Italian mail ships. Then it goes to Marseille via Spain, and then to Southampton. Shanghai mail ships directly reach Southampton, connecting to Atlantic mail ships, which is an innovation.

Bicycle Manufacturers Association Requests the Finance Bureau to Improve License Fees 167

The Shanghai Bicycle Manufacturers Association submitted a request to the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, saying: This is a request. It says in the Municipal Public Works Bureau's Notice No. 226 that each bicycle should pay a license fee of 5 jiao, which is 3 yuan for the whole year, etc. Compared with the donation rate in previous years, it has increased by one yuan. After reading it, the members of the association all believed that in March last year, after the concession's Public Works Bureau announced an increase in bicycle license fees, they had explained the reasons and requested a quarterly reduction to show fairness. The concession's Public Works Bureau approved it, and from January 1, 1935, those who obtained a license would pay a full-year donation of 4 yuan, and those who obtained a license from July 1 would pay a donation of 2 yuan, which was reduced in installments. Now that the bicycle license donation in this city has also increased by one yuan, I don't know if the collection method is reduced in installments. Please present the previous situation, etc. According to this, the donation rate, whether large or small, should be based on the principle of equality. The license donation for any vehicle, whether collected quarterly or monthly, and there are regulations for returning the license and sending the donation for motor vehicle licenses, but it is unfair to collect the full year for bicycle license donations. Not only do passengers suffer the sacrifice of retroactivity, but the same industry association has more impact on sales in autumn and winter. Now that the bureau's increase in bicycle license donations is the same as that of the concession's Public Works Bureau, the collection method should not be different. Therefore, I would like to explain the previous situation and submit it to the bureau for review. I hope that the installments will be reduced in installments and quickly followed, which is convenient for the public. Respectfully presented to the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau.

McNaughton Recounts His Encounter with Robbers on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway 168

The Robbers Were Skilled at Checking, Seemingly with Another Purpose, and Received Courteous Treatment from Chairman Huang and Others After Arriving in Hangzhou

According to the Zi Lin Bao, McNaughton, the Deputy General Manager of the Public Works Bureau, returned to Shanghai from Hangzhou yesterday (the 14th). He said that he was indeed robbed on the way to Hangzhou last Friday morning, but the incident was accidental and not unusual. Zhejiang Chairman Huang Shaoxiong had entrusted the British Consul-General in Shanghai to arrange a meeting in Hangzhou, so he set off by car on Friday morning with a Chinese colleague. The journey was smooth, and at about 20 minutes past noon yesterday, he drove between Haining and Haiyan. He was tired and leaned against the corner of the car for a nap. Suddenly, he was awakened by a gunshot. At that time, the driver had slowed down the car, and then he saw a Chinese man with a pistol approaching the side of the car, so the car stopped. Then he saw another Chinese man with a pistol approaching from ten yards away. The first man ordered the driver to get out of the car and search his body and the front of the car. Then he touched McNaughton's outer clothing with his hand. According to McNaughton, the man seemed to be skilled at checking, and his purpose seemed to be something else, not just loose change. The searcher then asked the Chinese in the car for money. McNaughton carried two rolls of banknotes, one only about 40 yuan, and the other 100 yuan, so he took out the smaller one and handed it over. The man seemed satisfied and robbed the driver of 13 yuan and the Chinese in the car of 30 yuan. Although there were villagers watching from a distance, they did not come to help or catch the robbers. After the two robbers had finished robbing, they ordered the car to turn back and drove back about half a mile to a certain place, where they made a phone call to inform the stationmaster of Haining to warn other passengers arriving at the station. At that time, the Deputy Commissioner of Commerce of the Canadian Government and a friend happened to arrive at the station by car, and they were strongly urged not to move forward. McNaughton waited for about 20 minutes and decided to take the risk and continue to move forward. He finally arrived in Hangzhou at 2:30 pm, only one hour late. At that time, all police stations had received news of the robbery and were arresting the car. McNaughton then met with the chairman, mayor, etc., and received courteous treatment, and they were very concerned about McNaughton's experience on the way. When McNaughton left Hangzhou, the county magistrate personally sent him to the county boundary, with very thorough protection. It is suspected that the robbers must have received advance notice that opium or other valuables were passing through the area and mistakenly intercepted McNaughton's car, not intending to rob money.

International Trade Bureau Introduces New York's Need for Pig Bristles 169

Exporters Can Contact the Bureau

Pig bristles are the hair that grows on the back of pigs, as hard as needles, about two to seven inches long. The quality depends on the origin and slaughter period, the length and color of the bristles. Generally, those produced in cold regions are better than those produced in temperate regions, and those obtained during the spring slaughter period are better than those obtained during the autumn slaughter period. Long and white ones are more expensive than short and black ones. Wild boar bristles are even more valuable than domestic pig bristles. Most of them are used to make brushes, and white bristles can also be used as raw materials for toothbrushes, hat brushes, etc. Every year, a large number of them are transported from Mongolia, Northeast China, North China, and provinces in the Yangtze River Basin to the United Kingdom, France, and the United States. Tianjin, Chongqing, and Hankou are the export centers. The products produced in Sichuan are of excellent quality and are most welcome in the European market. Now, the West Duenus Import and Export Company in New York, USA, has sent a letter requesting pig bristles and rice ears for brush making. I hope that exporters will send a letter to the bureau's guidance office for introduction.

Hua Dong Bank Manager Pang Feng-zhi Accused 178

Embezzlement Discovered After Closure, Lawsuit Filed by Chairman and Directors

The Ningbo Road Hua Dong Commercial Savings Bank, since its establishment, has been in operation for several years, with Pang Feng-zhi serving as manager. Last year, due to business losses amounting to hundreds of thousands of dollars, it could not be maintained and was declared insolvent. The chairman, Sun Bo-sheng, and directors Wu Fu-kang, Lu Xu-dong, and others are in charge of the liquidation, with each shareholder bearing full responsibility for repaying the debts. At the same time, the debts owed to others are being recovered separately. Now, as a result of the liquidation by liquidators Sun Bo-sheng and others, it has been discovered that manager Pang Feng-zhi has engaged in embezzlement and breach of trust, with the amount of embezzlement reaching tens of thousands of dollars. Therefore, they have hired lawyer Chen Ting-rui to file a complaint with the Criminal Court of the First Special District Court, accusing Pang of violating Articles 357 and 356 of the Criminal Law, and including civil proceedings, demanding the return of US$49,670.56 plus agreed interest up to the date of repayment, and the return of a Ford car. The points of fraud and embezzlement listed total more than five, which are recorded separately below: (1) A person with the same name as the reporter deposited 50,000 yuan in face value of 19-year Customs Treasury Bonds for US$14,300 on January 27 of the 23rd year, owing principal and interest of US$15,386.02 by the end of November. It has now been discovered that the mortgaged Treasury Bonds have disappeared and have been replaced by 25,000 yuan in original public debt notes that do not repay principal or interest. It was also found that after obtaining the address of the person with the same name as the reporter, a letter was sent to inquire, but it was returned by the post office, indicating that this person with the same name as the reporter is actually Pang's alias. (2) On October 30 of the 20th year, Wang Fu-ji used 10,000 yuan in 20-year cigarette Treasury Bonds, 10,000 yuan in 20-year Customs Treasury Bonds, and 5,000 yuan in 19-year Rehabilitation Treasury Bonds as collateral for overdraft borrowing, with a term of three months, overdrawing US$7,000. Subsequently, on January 4, the Rehabilitation Treasury Bonds were taken away, and 10,000 yuan in 20-year Consolidated Tax Treasury Bonds were deposited. After the expiration date, it was extended for another six months, expiring on July 31 of the 23rd year. Now, checking the accounts, it is found that all the Treasury Bonds have been taken away, and two worthless papers of the Tian Dan have been deposited. When Wang Lin-ji was urged to pay, he ignored it. The defendant has neither cleared the debt to Wang Lin-ji nor allowed him to illegally take out the collateral. This is collusion by the defendant, which is difficult to deny. (3) A household named Pang Lu-ji, for credit overdraft, has no contract to check. As of the end of November last year, the debt was US$12,134.30. Now, a thorough search of the household's real name and address reveals that there is no such person, which is a fabrication of the defendant and is actually the defendant's alias. (4) Heng De household is also an overdraft with credit, without a contract for verification. By the end of November of the 23rd year, the outstanding principal and interest were US$7,493.46. The funds of this household are without basis and cannot be recovered to this day. (5) According to bank practice, there is no suspense account item, but it is now found that there is a suspense account item that reaches a huge amount of 8,300 yuan. The payment vouchers cannot be found, making it impossible to recover. (6) On August 10 of the 20th year, Hua Dong Bank purchased a Ford car from the Meitong Company, as stated in notes No. 4356 and No. 5731, for internal office use. Unexpectedly, after Pang Feng-zhi resigned, he did not return the car. Despite repeated requests, he ignored them. This case was heard in the Criminal Court No. 8 of the First Special Court by Judge Wu Ting-qi yesterday afternoon. The defendant, Pang Feng-zhi, did not attend due to illness, and lawyer Gao Jun-xiang attended the court and requested a postponement of the trial. After the court briefly questioned Sun Bo-sheng and the other two, lawyer Chen Ting-rui agreed to the defendant's request for an adjournment. Judge Wu then ordered that the case be adjourned for one week for another hearing.

Skull Gang Extorts Zhou Qian-kang 179

Initially Demanding Five Thousand, Then Increasing to Eight Thousand, Visiting in Person, Finally Arrested

Zhou Qian-kang, manager of the Shanghai Brewery Company, lives at 159 Kang Nao Tuo Road in West Shanghai, and his family is quite wealthy. He usually employs Li Bao-sheng as a bodyguard and employs a Chinese constable No. 1941 as a watchman at home. Unexpectedly, at 5:30 PM on the 6th of this month, Zhou received a threatening letter signed by the Skull Gang, demanding US$5,000 and arranging for a Wu Tian-lin to go to collect the money on the 10th. Unexpectedly, on the 10th, Wu Tian-lin did not go to Zhou's house. Only at 4:00 PM that afternoon, a telephone call was received asking if Zhou was at home. After Zhou's wife told him that Zhou had gone out, the phone was disconnected. On the 11th at 2:00 PM, another letter was received, increasing the amount of extortion to US$8,000. The letter also arranged to make contact by phone at 10:00 AM on the 13th and send someone to collect the money at 2:00 PM that afternoon. On the 13th, there was no phone call, only a Sun Zu-de came to visit Zhou. Because Zhou had gone out, the watchman told him that he had gone out. Sun then took a business card and gave it to the constable, saying that he would come again at 11:00 AM tomorrow. Zhou reported to the Gordon Road Police Station, and Chinese detective Zhu Han-bo and detective Zhao Qing-kui went to Zhou's house to wait. On the 14th at 3:00 PM, Sun Zu-de again called Zhou's house to inquire about Zhou's whereabouts. Detective Zhu pretended to be Zhou Qian-kang and told him that the money should be paid, but the amount should be reduced, and asked him to come to collect it at 5:00 or 6:00 PM. The detectives wrapped white paper into the shape of banknotes, waiting for Sun to come and collect it. Before long, Sun actually came. The watchman handed the paper package to him. Just as he was unpacking it, the detectives stepped forward and arrested him, taking him back to the police station. Sun confessed that he was from Changshu. There was also a Sun Zhong-xin, 22 years old, who currently lives in Room 43 of the Liangxi Hotel on Hubei Road. He admitted that he wrote the threatening letters. Yesterday morning, the police station lawyer Zhang Tian-yin prosecuted him for extortion under Article 370 of the Criminal Law. Because further investigation was needed, he requested a postponement. Sun Zu-de confessed, "I knew Zhou Qian-kang when I was in middle school. Now, because I have been unemployed for a long time and my livelihood is difficult, I did this illegal thing." Judge Wu Ting-qi verified the confession and then ordered the case to be adjourned for another hearing.

Beikou Sand Ship Sunk by Western Steamer 182

Sunk Midships, Sixteen People Missing

The Beikou sand ship You Zhenxing, recently loaded with more than a thousand salted pigs purchased by Shanghai merchants Yi Tai Yuan Ji Yong Cheng and others, as well as yellow sprouts and other goods, at Qingkou and Liangxiang in Shandong and was heading to Shanghai to unload. Because the goods were urgently needed for sale, the ship owner, Peng Rong, was instructed to sail quickly so that they could arrive in Shanghai and sell them as soon as possible. After the ship was loaded, Peng ordered the crew to raise anchor and sail with three-masted sails, traveling day and night. On the day before yesterday, when sailing to the ocean about ten miles east of Dongtai, there was fog, but the route could still be identified. Later, the fog gradually thickened, and the route became difficult to identify. The crew informed the ship owner, Peng, who came out of the cabin to inspect and instructed the helmsman to steer towards the coast and anchor to avoid the fog. Just as the helmsman was turning the rudder, a whistle was heard. The crew looked and saw a steamer approaching directly from a distance of more than ten feet. Not knowing which ship it was, they immediately turned the rudder to avoid it. However, the steamer was traveling fast and had already reached the bow of the ship, crashing violently into the You Zhenxing amidships, causing it to break apart, flood, and gradually sink. All the people on the ship fell into the water and called for help. After the steamer stopped, it lowered a sampan to rescue them. Twelve people were rescued and transported by the steamer to Dongtai Port. A small boat was hired to ferry the twelve rescued people ashore and given US$20. The steamer then sailed away. The rescued crew members reported the incident to Yi Tai and others in Shanghai yesterday on the Haimen steamer, requesting assistance and seeking negotiations with the steamer. According to the crew members, there were a total of twenty-eight people on the ship. Twelve of us were rescued by the offending steamer, but sixteen others, including the ship owner Peng and the accountant, are missing. It is not known if they have been rescued. In the afternoon, after the steamer rescued us, it sailed to Dongtai. At night, a small boat was hired to ferry us ashore, so we were unable to identify the type of ship. The companies are now asking people to investigate the ships that entered and exited that day in order to negotiate.

Postal Administration Announces Reduced Parcel Rates for Chengdu and Above 186

Shanghai Postal Administration Announcement No. 1196 states: It has been found that parcels sent to Chengdu and above and transported by Yu-Cheng (Chongqing to Chengdu) automobiles are subject to an additional pure fee, as notified in Announcements Nos. 1164 and 1165. Effective immediately, this additional fee will be temporarily reduced to half a pure fee. Starting from the date of the fee reduction, for all parcels sent to Chengdu and above, unless the sender clearly states that they do not want the parcels to be transported by Yu-Cheng automobiles and are still charged according to the current rate, the bureau will uniformly charge according to the Yu-Cheng automobile transport parcel rate (i.e., according to the current Suining Road rate, plus a pure fee) to expedite delivery. This announcement is hereby made for general knowledge.

Tong Cheng Steamer Collides with Lighter 187

Company Investigating

The Tong Cheng steamer, Tong Cheng, owned by Tong Cheng Company on Jiangxi Road, with a load of 3,000 tons, arrived in Shanghai with coal on the 13th and was berthed at the Beipiao Wharf for unloading. Yesterday at around 2:00 PM, the unloading was completely finished, and the steamer left the wharf and headed to the No. 20 river cylinder on the Yangshupu River to anchor, preparing to load a large batch of flour for Tianjin. However, shortly after leaving the wharf and traveling north and east in the Huangpu River, a lighter carrying goods was traveling south in the Huangpu River. When approaching Tong Cheng, due to the strong wind and rapid tide, when it drove up to the steamer, the lighter was unable to avoid it, resulting in the ship being hit by the Tong Cheng steamer. The ship was damaged and about to sink. Fortunately, the boatmen inside the ship were rescued. The Tong Cheng still sailed to the No. 20 river cylinder and anchored. The shipowner reported to the company. The company then sent people on board to investigate the truth of the matter and examine the damage to the lighter to serve as a basis for handling negotiations.

Severe Cold Weather and Strong Winds Cause Two Fires 191

Two Women Responsible for the Fires Have Been Interrogated Separately

At around 2:00 AM yesterday morning, a fire broke out in the home of Zhang Qian, a young woman from Yancheng (42 years old) residing at No. 2, Fengji Lane, Fengji Wharf in the South City. The fire was caused by a candle flame spreading to straw. At the time, the northwest wind was raging. The fire quickly penetrated the roof. After the nearby police officer learned of the incident, he immediately notified the Dongjiadu and other fire brigades by telephone. He quickly drove a pump and belt vehicle to the scene. After the firefighters tried their best to put out the fire, it was extinguished in about an hour. A total of three thatched houses were burned down. Afterwards, the Dongjiadu Police Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau dispatched police officers to investigate the cause of the fire and took the arsonist Zhang Qian to the police station for interrogation. Furthermore, at 1:30 AM yesterday morning, a fire also broke out at Xieyuan Meat Store and Shuanglong Hotel at Nos. 74 and 76 Gonghe Road in Zhabei due to overturning a kerosene stove. When the Zhabei fire brigades were notified and arrived at the scene, the fire had already spread due to the strong northerly wind. The fire was extinguished by the firefighters at around 3:00 AM. A total of two buildings were burned down. It is heard that the arsonist, Cheng Chen, has been arrested and interrogated by the Xinzha Sub-bureau.

Shen Zhen-hua, Director of the Lao Beimen Police Station of the Public Security Bureau, issued a notice in order to implement the New Life Movement, stating: "For notification purposes, this office has repeatedly received instructions from the Public Security Bureau and official letters from the Health Bureau, stating that Shanghai is a place of great importance to Chinese and foreign observers, and it is imperative to rectify the city's appearance and earnestly implement the New Life Movement. Extreme measures must be taken to rectify the traffic and sanitation on major thoroughfares. If the subordinates fail to implement them effectively, and the residents openly defy them, they will be subject to appropriate punishment and heavy fines in accordance with the law, etc. Senior officials will personally inspect, supervise, and urge rectifications, not allowing any slackness. If there are deliberate violations, they will be punished immediately upon discovery, without any leniency." The matters that must be strictly observed are as follows: 1. All kinds of articles must not be piled outside the door or displayed along the road. 2. No work is allowed on the roadside or sidewalk. 3. No clothes are allowed to be dried on the street. 4. It is forbidden to arbitrarily pour sewage in front of the door and on the road. 5. It is forbidden to throw any debris in front of the door and on the road. 6. All kinds of vehicles are not allowed to be set up in violation of regulations. 7. The entrances of all shops and residents along the road must be swept and cleaned at any time every day. 8. No advertisements are allowed to be posted on the walls of all shops and residents' entrances. 9. The facades of all shops should be frequently washed and cleaned. 10. Extra attention should be paid to other traffic and sanitation violations.

Wei Haijiang Sues the Directors of the 儉德 Bank for Fraud, Embezzlement, and Malfeasance 196

The alleged fraudulent activities total five points. The trial was transferred to the local court for hearing yesterday.

The 儉德 Bank has been bankrupt for over a month, and there is still no way to repay its debts. The bank's director and manager, Chai Chuangui, has already been sued by creditors, and the case has not yet been concluded. Now, Wei Haijiang, a creditor who suffered a loss of more than 100,000 gold yuan due to the bank's bankruptcy, has hired lawyers Gao Junxiang and Yang Linzhi to file a criminal self-suit with the First Special District Local Court against Chai Chuangui and the chairman and directors of the bank's board of directors, Yan Ziyu, Xie Keming, Chen Xifu, Ma Huanzhi, Tu Kaizheng, Chai Yousheng, and the supervisor, Li Jingwei, for fraud, embezzlement, malfeasance, and breach of trust. They request severe punishment according to the law and also file a civil suit to recover their losses. The allegations against the defendants include

Facts of the Fraud 197

Totaling five points: (1) Chai Chuangui, knowing that Wei Haijiang had dealings with 儉德 Bank and was wealthy, instructed Gu Wensheng, the assistant manager of 儉德, to persuade Wei in June of last year, stating that the bank's capital was 1 million yuan, with 500,000 yuan already fully paid and registered, and that another 500,000 yuan was being raised, making the foundation solid and suitable for investment. Wei then paid 5,000 yuan on the 16th of that month. When the bank suspended operations on December 7th, Wei discovered that Gu's previous statements were entirely false. The bank's actual paid-up capital was only 100,000 yuan. Although it claimed to have raised 500,000 yuan when registering with the government, this was a fabrication, and there was no plan to increase capital. Gu's exaggeration was at Chai's instigation, hoping to

Induce Investment 198

(2) Wei had used American land deeds and three property title slips as collateral for overdrafts with the bank. In October of last year, Wei wanted to recover these slips, but they had already been pledged to 致祥莊 for 20,000 yuan. After Wei's negotiation, the bank redeemed them on December 3rd, but Chai pledged them again to the 四行儲蓄會 on the same day for 40,000 yuan, an additional 20,000 yuan more than the previous pledge, which has not yet been redeemed. (3) On October 23rd of last year, Chai, seeing that Wei Haijiang's trust in 儉德 had not waned, again sent Gu Wensheng to visit Wei, using the position of deputy manager as bait. Wei then met with Chai, who stated that he intended to develop the business and decided to hire Wei as deputy manager, requesting

Ways to Raise Funds 199

Wei, at Chai's request, mortgaged a land deed for 110 mu to Shanghai Bank in early November, borrowing 60,000 yuan, with Xie Keming as guarantor. All the funds were lent to 儉德. After obtaining the funds, Chai did not issue the promised letter of appointment as deputy manager, nor did he issue a formal document for the borrowed land deed. After repeated urging, Chai and the bank's directors and supervisors issued a private document, but the name of the chairman was not included. Only after the bank's bankruptcy did Wei realize that the bank's regulations only allowed for one deputy manager position, and Chai had no authority to appoint another. (4) Wei had an agreement with the bank for

Overdraft of 10,000 200

Yuan. If the overdraft did not exceed the agreed limit, the bank was required to honor Wei's checks without refusal. However, in late November, the bank repeatedly returned Wei's checks. Wei believes that his personal credit has suffered significant damage as a result, and the bank should be held liable for breach of trust. (5) Wei's purchase or acceptance of the company's shares as collateral is strictly prohibited by the company law, but the bank engaged in such actions in violation of Article 233 of the Company Law. In addition, the bank's false statements regarding

Discrepancies in Accounts 201

Are too numerous to mention. According to the law, the defendants are subject to criminal penalties, etc. The conclusion states that the defendants exploited the public's trust in banks, using the bank as a fraudulent institution. In recent months, banks such as 五華 and 中國興業 have closed one after another, and the actions of 儉德 show obvious signs of malfeasance. If they are not severely punished, the financial stability of society will be impossible. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ye Shengchao presided over the hearing of the case. Only three defendants, Chai Chuangui, Xie Keming, and Li Jingwei, appeared in court. The other defendants hired lawyers to defend them. First, the plaintiff's lawyer, Ye Shaoying, stated the reasons for the lawsuit. Then, Judge Ye briefly questioned the defendants Chai Chuangui and Xie Keming. Because this lawsuit does not fall within the jurisdiction of the primary court, he ordered it to be transferred to the local court for review.

Ministry of Education Supplementarily Announces Graduation Examination Subjects for Physical Education Teachers 215

The Ministry of Education, due to the request of the National Martial Arts Hall to promote martial arts, has included martial arts in the examination subjects and has supplemented the graduation examination subjects for physical education normal school students. It has issued an order to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to comply with it. Graduation examination subjects for physical education normal school students:

1. General Subjects: Civics, Chinese Language, History and Geography, Physics and Chemistry, Anatomy, Physiology, Introduction to Education.

2. Physical Education Subjects: A. Academic Subjects: Principles of Physical Education, Physical Education Administration; B. Technical Subjects: Track and Field, Gymnastics, Ball Games, Gymnastics, Floor Exercises, Martial Arts.

Male Gymnastics

Preparatory Standing Committee of the Chinese Art International Exhibition 220

Additional Committee Members Appointed to the Preparatory Committee

The Standing Committee of the Preparatory Committee for the Chinese Art International Exhibition has decided to solicit seven articles for the articles of the Goods Custody Committee: (1) This Custody Committee shall be organized with five to seven members. (2) The public and private goods solicited by the Preparatory Committee, except those that already have a preservation agency in Shanghai (such as the Palace Museum and the Ancient Artifacts Exhibition Hall, etc.), shall be stored in the bank vault designated by the Preparatory Committee. (3) The goods stored above shall be the responsibility of the Custody Committee, and shall not be withdrawn except during the exhibition period (including domestic previews and the London exhibition) and with the prescribed procedures. (4) The goods solicited by the Preparatory Committee shall be directly sent to the Custody Committee by the competent authority or the owner, and the Custody Committee shall hand them over to the designated bank for storage in the vault, and the bank shall sign a storage receipt to be collected and stored by the Custody Committee. (5) The goods stored in the vault must have a withdrawal form stamped by the Preparatory Committee, and must be stamped by the Custody Committee before they can be withdrawn. (6) The Preparatory Committee shall be responsible for matters such as goods insurance. (7) After the exhibition is over, the Custody Committee shall be responsible for promptly returning the goods to the various agencies or owners.

(Nanjing, 15th) The Preparatory Committee of the London Chinese Art International Exhibition has additionally appointed Zhang Yuquan as an advisor to the Specialized Committee, Wu Hufan and five others as members of the Custody Committee, and Lu Xirong, Li Dachao, and seven others as honorary secretaries, and has requested Mayor Wu of Shanghai to assist in guiding the progress of the preview to be held in Shanghai in March of this year.

(Jinan, 15th) The Provincial Library has decided to send the Western Zhou bronzes unearthed in Teng County last spring and the rubbings of Qin and Han bricks and tiles in the library's collection to the London Art Exhibition.

The Reading Classics Movement in Shantou Primary Schools 226

In addition to prohibiting mixed bathing for men and women, the Guangdong provincial authorities are also promoting the reading of classics in primary and secondary schools. This case was passed by the Southwest Political Affairs Conference in July of last year and transferred to the Department of Education to formulate reading classics measures, which were distributed to primary and secondary schools in various counties and cities, and will be implemented uniformly starting next semester. Shantou primary schools have not yet taught the classics due to a lack of teachers. Recently, Chen Zhongyu, the head of the municipal education section, specifically followed the instructions of Director Huang of the Department of Education to first organize a research society for primary school teachers to study the classics to train teachers to teach the classics, so that they can teach separately. The society has now been established, with Chen, the head of the education section, serving as the president, Wen Danming as the director, and Chen Mengqing and Wu Zhuming as lecturers. More than fifty people have already signed up to participate in the research. The opening ceremony was held in the auditorium of the Provincial Commercial School on the afternoon of January 4th. It is expected that research will begin in a few days. The reading materials compiled by the society are as follows: 1. Classic of Filial Piety, 2. Tang Xuanzong's Analects Reader, 3. Zheng Yiqing's Compilation of Mencius Zhu Zi's Annotations. Other classics such as the Doctrine of the Mean and the Great Learning will also be taught in succession. (Chen Changfeng, correspondent of this newspaper, January 9th)

Wang Yunwu's Thoughts on the Problem of China-Centered Cultural Construction 228

Since He Bingsong, Sun Hanbing, and ten other scholars in the domestic academic community recently published the declaration of China-centered cultural construction, it has attracted the attention of people across the country. In order to understand the attitudes of leaders from all walks of life towards this declaration, a reporter from the Shanghai News Agency specifically visited Mr. Wang Yunwu, the general manager of the Commercial Press, yesterday. He was granted an audience and expressed his extremely earnest attitude and extremely interesting remarks. Mr. Wang said at the outset, "I very much agree with the views of these scholars. I have the following thoughts on their views. Yesterday, at a banquet, a friend surnamed Zhao raised a statement that seemed like a joke, but in fact contained a profound truth. He said that their ancestor Zhao Pu, five hundred years ago, used half of the Analects to govern the world. He wondered whether it referred to the first half or the second half. He had doubts for a long time, and finally found an answer. The word 'half' should refer to a part. It probably means removing the unsuitable parts from the Analects and adopting the suitable parts. I think this answer is really correct. According to his answer, the saying '(half) of the Analects governs the world' can become a profound truth. Generally speaking, there must be a reason why books and doctrines can last for a long time, but one time is different from another. If we blindly follow the words of the ancients, there will inevitably be conflicts with the present. The Analects was produced more than a thousand years before Zhao Pu. If Zhao Pu did not ask about the situation of the Song Dynasty, and completely based his governance on the Analects, I am afraid the world would not be governed. Zhao Pu understood this principle and Song-ified the Analects, so he could achieve results and give credit to the Analects. But only half of the Analects, in other words, only a part of the Analects that was suitable for the Song Dynasty environment could govern the Song Dynasty. If it were the entire Analects, it would not have such good results. Now, a thousand years have passed since the Song Dynasty. Those who cling to the past still take 'it has been in ancient times' as a lesson, while those who like the new take 'it has been in Europe and America' as their mantra. Their mistakes are actually the same. I think that the people who want to use the Analects to govern the country now, the half of the Analects they should adopt, or a part of the Analects, must not be the same as Zhao Pu's half of the Analects. For the same reason, if we want to adopt the precedents of Europe and America to govern the country or handle affairs, we can only learn from Zhao Pu's method, and adopt a part of it that is suitable for our country. Let me give another example before us. Many people attribute the rapid recovery of the Commercial Press after the robbery to the scientific management methods that I brought back to China from Europe and America a few years ago. In fact, the scientific management methods that I am now implementing at the Commercial Press can be said to be very different from those prevalent in Europe and America, because I never blindly follow the scientific management methods of Europe and America, and have already Sinified it, especially Commercial Press-ified it. If not, not only may it not be effective, but there may also be many obstacles. Even a small matter is already like this, let alone national affairs and the entire culture, especially those that should not be blindly followed," and so on.

Three Important Cases Resolved and Implemented Separately

The Shanghai County Education Bureau held an administrative committee meeting the other day. General Meeting of the China Arts and Sciences Society 230

He Bingsong Elected as Chairman, Business Plan for This Year Determined

The China Arts and Sciences Society is a well-known academic organization in the country. Recently, in order to develop the society's affairs, it has revised its charter and made slight changes to its organization. Recently, it elected directors and organized a board of directors, and held a general meeting of directors the other day. Chuan Shishuo, Ma Zongrong, Pan Gongzhan, Chen Lifu (represented by Pan), Liu Baimin, He Bingsong, Bai Pengfei (represented by Chuan), Zheng Zhenwen, Tan Qinyu, and others, as well as alternate directors Zhang Menglin and Zhu Xianfang, etc., were present, which was sufficient for the legal quorum. Chuan Shishuo was elected as the temporary chairman to formally open the meeting.

Election of Chairman 231

As a result, He Bingsong was elected. The chairman then stood up and gave a speech, briefly stating that the society had a very glorious history in the past, and now has nearly a thousand members, all of whom are well-educated people in the country. Bingsong felt honored to be able to work together for the Chinese cultural cause. Regarding the future affairs of the society, according to his humble opinion, the main contribution should be to conduct specialized academic research and edit specialized works in various subjects. If we want to achieve this goal, it seems that the following tasks should be actively carried out: (1) Expanding the library, (2) Sorting out the original publications of the society, (3) Actively editing various specialized series. In short, since the society is an academic organization, it should of course continue to strive for academic work based on the society's purpose as the primary goal. Whether it is appropriate or not, I still hope that all directors will not hesitate to give advice, and hope that all members will guide us at any time, in order to seek the promotion and development of the society's affairs. Then, the former chairman Chuan Shishuo, the director of the General Affairs Department Liu Baimin, and the director of the Editorial Department Zhang Menglin, etc., reported on the society's financial affairs and editing situation respectively. Due to the late hour, it was decided to continue the meeting the next day.

Resolution of Various Important Cases 232

The general meeting of directors continued at 3:00 PM the next afternoon, discussing the implementation plan for various businesses this year. The more important resolutions are recorded as follows: (1) Enrich the library and aim to establish the Asian Library, the Chinese Library, the Japanese Library, the Members' Works Library, and the General Library, etc. (1) Sort out and carry out the editing of the National Renaissance Series, the Arts and Sciences Series, the Japanese Famous Works Series, the Arts and Sciences Compilation, and the compilation and printing of ancient books, etc. (2) Plan a plan for studying Chinese music (4) Establish a Natural Science Research Institute and a science experiment hall for middle schools, etc. At the same time, it was decided that Ma Zongrong, Pan Gongzhan, He Bingsong, and Chuan Shishuo would be responsible for presiding over the drafting of detailed plans for each case, and submit them to the next board of directors meeting for decision.

Appointment of Various Directors 233

In addition, according to the regulations, Cai Yuanpei, Wu Tiecheng, Wu Zhihui, Chen Guofu, Wang Shijie, He Yingqin, Song Ziwen, Ye Chuqiang, Wang Yunwu, Sun Ke, Qian Xinzhi, and other gentlemen, as well as Zhu Jiahua, Chen Lifu, Dai Jitao, Chuan Shishuo, Wang Zhaorong, Pan Gongzhan, Zheng Zhenwen, Hu Shuhua, Zhou Changshou, and Chen Daqi and other members of the society were appointed as directors, and the board of directors will send letters of appointment separately today. Liu Baimin and Zhu Zhangbao were appointed by the board of directors as the secretaries of the board of directors and the general director of the General Office, respectively. As for the annual meeting of this year, it was decided to hold it in Hankou in early April according to the decision of the general meeting, and the general director will start preparing immediately. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Strict Enrollment at Pudong Middle School 235

For the next semester's enrollment, Mr. Lin Zhongke, the principal of the school, acting in accordance with the wishes of the board of directors, advocated strictness and reducing the number of new students in order to improve the students' level and restore the glory of the school before the 16th year of the Republic. Expansion of Lixin Accounting School 236

Lixin Accounting Tutorial School, located at 190 Ningbo Road in this city, was founded by accountant Dr. Pan Xulun, and its purpose is to cultivate accounting practical talents for the industrial and commercial circles. It has been established for seven and a half years, and has two departments: correspondence and night school. Most of the students in the correspondence department are from other cities and cannot attend face-to-face lectures. The number of admissions has reached more than 2,800. The editing of accounting lecture notes, the correction of course papers, and the answering of questions are all very serious, so there is no difference from the effectiveness of face-to-face teaching. The courses currently offered, in addition to the original bookkeeping and elementary accounting, advanced accounting, banking accounting, and company accounting, three new courses have recently been added: Auditing, Complete Cost Accounting (to be taken after completing advanced accounting), and Simplified Cost Accounting (to be taken after completing bookkeeping elementary accounting), to prepare for the study of internal audit by those from other cities who are interested in internal audit in various industrial and commercial institutions and cost accounting in various manufacturing plants. The department enrolls students all year round, and they can enroll at any time.

Also, the night school department makes use of evening leisure time, making it convenient for accounting staff who are already employed in this city and students of vocational schools who are still studying. The number of graduates from previous sessions has reached more than 3,200. Shanghai is the most developed area of accounting academics in China. In recent years, the demand for accounting talents from various industrial and commercial institutions has increased even more. As a result, the number of people who go to the school to apply for admission has also increased sharply year by year. Only because the school's address is limited and the classrooms are cramped, although it tries to enroll nearly 400 people each term, there are still no less than one or two hundred people who cannot be accommodated. It is reported that in order to remedy this shortcoming, the school has additionally opened several spacious classrooms on the upper floors of the Xinhua Bank at the intersection of Jiangxi Road and Ningbo Road, and decided to add classes starting next term to accommodate them. In addition, the school's class time was originally from 7:00 PM to 9:00 PM every night. This time is quite inconvenient for those who have no duties after 5:00 PM. It is reported that starting next term, an early class will be added, with classes from 5:30 PM to 7:15 PM, so that scholars who finish their duties at various institutions early can go to school first and then return home to rest. The current term of the school is about to end, and the next term is scheduled to start on February 11th. Jiangsu Social Education Facilities (2) 242

(Report by Zhou Fohai, Director of the Jiangsu Education Department, at the Provincial Government Memorial Week)

Secondly, the work of formulating standards for social education: In the past, the work of various social education institutions lacked standards, either avoiding difficulties and seeking ease without considering effectiveness, or engaging in extravagant displays to dazzle the public. As a result, there were no achievements. To remedy this drawback, it was necessary to stipulate work standards for various social education institutions. Therefore, in the 21st year, standard work for public education centers and farmer education centers was formulated, ordering social education institutions in each county to earnestly comply and to formulate scoring sheets for each county bureau to earnestly investigate the implementation of standard work in the 21st year. The situation and results of the examination have been written as a special article and published in Jiangsu Education. At the beginning of the 22nd year, the standards of various social education institutions were revised, and (Measures for Popularizing Public Education by Central Institutions in Public Education Zones in Each County) were separately formulated, stipulating that each institution must divide the entire public education zone into basic education zones and promotion zones, and that each institution must popularize standard work within the basic education zone within two years. Now, each institution has been in the basic education zone for a year. The implementation is still good. The result will be compiled into a detailed report during the general examination next year.

Thirdly, social education in each county is to be divided into zones for guidance: The establishment and work standards of social education institutions in each county have already been stipulated, but how the implementation is going must be inspected and guided. Therefore, it is stipulated that in addition to provincial school inspectors and county school inspectors and education committee members inspecting social education institutions in each county on schedule, the entire province will be divided into six public education zones, with provincial social education institutions responsible for guiding social education institutions in each county. Because the establishment of provincial social education institutions is, on the one hand, to study and experiment with methods for implementing social education, and on the other hand, to assume the responsibility of guiding local social education. This method has been implemented since the 22nd year, and the results of the implementation have been quite satisfactory. At the same time, it is also stipulated that provincial social education institutions must convene regional social education research conferences organized by social institutions in each county to further enhance the research interest of social education service personnel.

Fourthly, the active promotion of literacy education and livelihood education: The number of illiterate people in China accounts for more than 10%, resulting in low public intelligence and a decline in public morale. The implementation of social guidance must naturally pay special attention to literacy education. In addition, China's production is backward, the people's livelihood is extremely dilapidated, and the rural economy is even more desolate. Social education facilities must naturally pay considerable attention to livelihood education. Therefore, when we formulated the standard work for the 21st year, we stipulated that social education institutions should focus on literacy education and livelihood education. At the same time, we also formulated two specific plans: a concrete plan for promoting public schools in each county within three years, and a concrete plan for social education institutions to promote livelihood education, and ordered them to be followed. Regarding the specific plan for promoting public schools in each county within three years, except for a few counties that failed to comply due to economic concerns, most counties implemented it accordingly. The number of public schools and students in each county has increased sharply compared to before, which is the reason. As for the specific plan for livelihood education, due to talent and economic factors, it has not yet been fully implemented and will be promoted in the future.

Fifthly, pay attention to the assessment and protection of the heads of social education institutions: The heads of social education institutions are the leaders of social education institutions. Whether social education can be promoted and whether standard work can be effectively implemented is closely related to whether the heads of institutions are competent. If the head of the institution is competent, the planning and execution of the cause will surely be twice the result with half the effort; otherwise, it will inevitably be perfunctory. Therefore, since the promulgation of the standard work, the assessment of the heads of social education institutions has also been given great attention. The heads of institutions who are already in office must be strictly assessed, and those who are about to take office or are preparing to take office must also be given a strict assessment in advance. All counties recommend the heads of social education institutions, and they are first ordered to come to the department for talks in order to examine them. During the examination, in addition to paying attention to their academic knowledge and experience, special attention is paid to their social experience, educational ideals, work interest, and methods of handling affairs. They must have experience in society, have ideals for education, have interest in work, and have methods for handling affairs in order to endure hardship and go deep into the people to work; otherwise, they cannot be appointed. In addition, the county magistrates and bureau chiefs in each county often arbitrarily appoint and dismiss the heads of social education institutions due to personal disagreements, so that the heads of social education institutions cannot stay in their positions for a long time and naturally cannot work with peace of mind. Therefore, each county is also notified to earnestly protect the heads of social education institutions, and all appointments and dismissals must be submitted for approval, and each county must not handle them without authorization, so that the heads of each social education institution can work with peace of mind.
