Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise 243

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seven Carefully Inquiring About the Eastern Section

This scholar clapped his hands on his thigh, stood up, turned half a circle, and said with a slight stumble: Your words are truly thorough. Saying this, his face straightened, and he looked at Zhiqian and said: Just now, Mr. Cheng said that Yuan Youwei, is he the Director of the Department of Finance? Cheng Zhiqian smiled and said: Of course it is him. If he wasn't the Director of the Department of Finance, would the Director of the Department of Construction be willing to welcome his brother? Li Shilian said: Director Gao is inviting Director Yuan's brother to dinner, with Mr. Cheng as a guest. Needless to say, Mr. Cheng is very familiar with both sides. Cheng Zhiqian smiled slightly and did not reply. Seeing this, Li Shilian was certain that their friendship had reached a considerable degree, and sat silently on the side, thinking only about the truth of the matter. He was thinking to himself, and he didn't know how many minutes he had been silent. When he woke up and looked forward, he saw Wang Beihai holding a book and walking towards Zhiqian. He understood in his heart that this was someone tutoring. If he were sensible, he should leave and not disturb them here. Even if he had something to say, he should wait until this person had finished his homework before speaking. Doing so would win their favor. Thinking that this was right, he stood up, gave Zhiqian a half bow, and said with a smile: Don't delay Mr. Wang's tutoring. See you later. Saying that, he walked towards the door. Looking back, he saw that Zhiqian was also by his side, so he bent down, held his fists, and arched his hands several times. He didn't dare to suddenly turn around, but kept backing away, retreating to a place where Zhiqian couldn't see him in the house. He kept looking forward, being polite to people, not thinking that he was backing up to the edge of the corridor, and colliding with the corridor pillar. With a thud, his spine was almost numb. Fortunately, there was no one in the courtyard, and he held back his tears and stood there for a while. Zhang Jiefu, who lived next door to him, stuck his head out and looked at him. Seeing him standing there, he thought he was thinking about something and was lost in thought. (113)

Random Notes on Banknotes 245

— Xu Xiaoting

Using a colorful piece of paper circulating in society, grasping the source of circulating finance, the greatness of banknotes, we live if we get them, and die if we don't. What we hear and see, and the facts that are passed down, are recorded randomly for after-dinner conversation.

The color of banknotes varies depending on the issuing bank. According to some comedians, red represents the blood and sweat of laborers and farmers, crimson represents beautiful women, green represents China's agricultural foundation and the need for greening, and gray represents the faces of general coolies.

My deceased friend Yin Qingguang had a line about banknotes: "Coming from a piece of paper, originally empty, Kuriroku fiercely competes for it." Another line said: "Bright as a beauty in red and green, not caring about changing allegiances morning and night." The words contain deep meaning and are worth reading.

I once saw in the bedroom of a wealthy young man, the flower paper that should have been pasted on the wall was replaced with banknotes. His method of pasting was to use white silk paper as the base and paste banknotes on it. He did not brush paste, but used pins to stick them. The banknotes themselves were not damaged in the slightest. The colorful sight could be called spectacular. But the golden and silver air is overpowering, and it is not as elegant as a book and a painting adorning the wall.

My relative Yin Peijun once told me something. He said that a student Wang in a certain school in Shanghai, one night gambled with his lover, using banknotes as paper to blow, and setting fire to them for fun. In an instant, dozens of pieces were burned. Wang was the son of a wealthy merchant and regarded money as dirt. Although his lover tried to stop him, Wang didn't care. Such a waste of natural resources, I fear, has reduced a lot of good fortune in the dark.

Subsidiary currency notes are lower-grade banknotes, and their wide circulation carries a universal color. Because of the frequency of circulation, they are easily damaged. Recently, the subsidiary currency notes circulating in the market are mostly dirty and worn out. A note is divided into several pieces, but still used together. People in the common class often call them "broken cloth notes" in a homophonic pun, which is extremely funny.

The form of ghost money is indeed no different from that of banknotes. Illiterate countrymen in Jiangbei and inland areas are often fooled by it. Therefore, when countrymen use banknotes, they are both afraid of them being fake and afraid of them being ghost money. They do not regard banknotes as affectionately as silver dollars.

Modern Marvels 246

— Dehong

Teachers and friends are everywhere, but their words and deeds are different. I dare to introduce one or two of those I know.

A certain chemistry teacher at a certain middle school, Mr. So-and-so, explained Yeast as 酵母 (xiào mǔ), but (酵) was mistakenly read as (xiào), and the sound of "filial mother" (孝母) was heard everywhere, which can be said to be a source of great fun.

My classmate Mr. Zhu, being in mourning at home, one day wrote a letter to his classmate at the same desk, inquiring about the recent situation at school, signing his name as Zhu Zhi XX. When he received the reply, he couldn't help but burst out laughing before he had even opened it. The crowd didn't understand, and asked to see it. The envelope said: (Mr. Zhu Zhi XX Receives) (This matter was personally told to me by Mr. Zhu).

Mr. So-and-so is eloquent, lively, and especially good at socializing, and is known as a socialite. He once asked me with extremely polite formalities: (Where does your father work?) I was stunned.

My classmate Mr. So-and-so, returned to his hometown to get married. He only returned to Shanghai three weeks later. After I found out about this, I announced it in public. Mr. Yang asked me: (Did you bring your wife out?) I answered as if I didn't know, but I knew that he had backfired and made a mess of things.

Records of Lingering Fragrance 247

— Original work by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Starting from a place more than ten zhang away, there were many bamboo poles, standing tall and short: the tallest was taller than a person, and the shortest was only half a foot from the ground. And the thickness of these bamboo poles themselves was also different... the thickest was thicker than a person's arm, and the thinnest was only the size of a thumb. Their styles were even more peculiar: some were straight, some were curved, some were pointed at the top, and some were tied with a ring. Their distances were also absolutely not uniform, starting from places ten or so zhang away, all the way to the edge of the white wall at the very end, both near and far. When we saw it, we were simply bewildered. We could only stare with our eyes wide open, and we didn't know where to start asking!

(This is the arrow range! Those standing bamboo poles are all targets used by people practicing archery.) So the Empress Dowager automatically explained to us. (The emperors of all dynasties and the close ministers who accompanied them on hunts often came here to practice. Each person took turns shooting, three arrows each time; and each time they had to identify a different bamboo pole as the target. They had to make sure that all three arrows hit the target. Generally speaking, among these bamboo poles, those that are far away, and those that are very tall, very short, or curved, are more difficult to hit. One must first practice from those that are near, straight, and neither too high nor too low, progressing gradually from easy to difficult. When one practices to the point where one can hit any bamboo pole with three arrows in a row, this person's archery skills can be considered to have reached the peak; the results of the seasonal hunt will undoubtedly be very good! And his fame will surely spread throughout the country and be admired by people.)

We did not walk onto the arrow range, but only stood at the door and looked from a distance. The two iron rings hanging in the air with ropes behind us, and these two doors, were probably only three or four steps away, directly opposite the center of this door frame. The Empress Dowager turned around and pointed to these two iron rings and said: (223)

A City of Flesh and Blood 248

Vegetable Prices After the Famine 249

— Jiaoxin

Every year between the tenth and eleventh months of the lunar calendar is when families in the mainland pickle vegetables. This year, the various vegetables are particularly cheap. Green vegetables are four to five hundred cash per dan, snow cabbage is one thousand cash per dan, radishes are eight hundred cash per dan, and large mustard greens (i.e., large mustard cabbage) are one cent of a dollar each. This cheap price is said to have broken the record for many years. Then it should be good news for the poor, but it is not. Precisely because the vegetables are particularly cheap, it is even more harmful to the farmers, leaving them with no way to make a living.

This year, the drought has caused disaster. The rice planted by the farmers has all dried up. For the time being, other grains cannot be planted in the fields, so everyone grows vegetables. Therefore, the yield has exceeded that of previous years, so supply exceeds demand, and prices have fallen sharply. According to the farmers, such cheap prices do not even cover the cost. When it comes to selling, because there are few people, and they have to hire people to help carry them into the city to sell, the city people do not need so many vegetables. They cannot sell them as soon as they are carried into the city as in previous years, so they have to carry them to the streets and alleys to solicit customers from door to door. Therefore, by the time they are sold, it is already late, and the price they get is barely enough to eat a meal in the city. There is little left, not even enough for the workers' wages, let alone making a profit.

Logically, with vegetables so cheap, city people should buy more than in previous years: but the facts are not entirely so. Because the price of salt in recent years has been increasing year by year, and now it costs more than four hundred cash per shi jin. For example, pickling one dan of green vegetables requires four or five jin of salt, which adds up to two thousand cash. After the great drought this year, commerce has become even more sluggish due to the bankruptcy of the countryside. City people, of course, are mostly merchants. Even if they are worried about the necessities of food and clothing, they have no spare capacity to consider the future. Therefore, no matter how cheap the vegetables are, and because of the high price of salt, most people are unable to afford them.

Small Horticulture

Vassals of the Fragrant Kingdom 250

— Zheng Yimei

(1) Rohdea japonica

Rohdea japonica, also known as millennium plant, is a perennial evergreen herb. The leaves are thick and large, growing in clusters from underground stems. The flower stems grow from the center of the leaf clusters, four or five inches long. The flowers are light green, and the fruits are crimson and lovely. There are also yellow ones that do not wither after a long time, hence the name.

It is planted in pots by cutting during the vernal equinox and autumnal equinox. It likes shade and moisture.

Watering with leftover cold black tea juice is most suitable.

In Wu customs, families plant Rohdea japonica in their gardens, mainly to observe the prosperity and decline of the Rohdea japonica, in order to predict the prosperity and decline of the family's fortune. Moreover, for all moving, betrothal, and all joyous events, it must be prepared to bring good luck. Even if fresh ones are not available, satin must be cut to resemble its shape to replace it. On the fourteenth day of the fourth month of the lunar calendar, the birthday of the immortals. Women often go to remove old leaves on the night of the day before, and scatter them in the alleyways, saying that the immortals are playing in the world and accidentally trampling on them, which will bring good omens, and new leaves will sprout and naturally grow beautifully.

(2) Chlorophytum

Zhuangzi said: Emptiness generates white, and auspiciousness stops. The plant that takes its name from it is Chlorophytum. This grass grows naturally in wetlands. The stems extend close to the ground, and the leaves grow in clusters on it, resembling orchids. They are more than a foot long, narrow and pointed, with parallel veins, and are evergreen in all seasons. Under the clusters of leaves, roots and beards grow again. Fine flowers bloom in summer, white inside and purple outside. It is often planted together with Rohdea japonica in family gardens and courtyards, but it is rare to see it blooming, and seeing it brings good fortune.

It can be divided and cut after rain, and nine out of ten will survive. It is especially elegant to accompany solitary rocks and ganoderma.

(3) Liriope graminifolia

My friend, the desert poet, once compared monk shoes, chrysanthemums, and Liriope graminifolia to my essays. Liriope graminifolia comes from the place where Zheng Kangcheng read books in Zichuan County, Shandong Province. It was originally my family's thing. The poet's metaphor can be said to be accurate.

Liriope graminifolia, also known as Xiudun grass, is also known as Mai Dong. The leaves are like chives, more than a foot long, soft and clustered, fresh and lovely. It does not wither even in winter. Short flower stems grow in the center, blooming with light purple fine flowers. Planting it on the courtyard steps, it hangs down on all sides, suitable for clear play. The fruits are round and blue. There are also small white fruits on the roots. If you take it, wash it, and soak it in boiling water, you can use it as tea. It tastes delicious and sweet, and it is cool in nature, and has the effect of treating throat diseases.

(4) Ilex chinensis

Ilex chinensis is clustered, evergreen in all seasons, and can be trimmed to form hedges. If planted in mountainous areas, it can grow freely and can be as high as a zhang. The leaves are oval, light at the ends, alternate, thick and glossy. Small white flowers bloom in early summer. Male flowers are clustered inflorescences, and female flowers grow in the leaf axils. The fruits are red and small, like red beans, which are different from the long leaves and black fruits of Ligustrum lucidum. It grows from the ground as soon as it is pressed, and is easy to transplant and survive. If you want it to be lush, you must use dog feces to fertilize it. The bark of those with small leaves can be used to make glue to catch birds, called small-leaf Ilex chinensis.

Ilex chinensis is also known as evergreen branch. Emperor Huizong of the Song Dynasty tested the students of the Painting Academy, using "Peaceful Birds on Evergreen Branches" as the topic, but no one knew it, because the name was very unpopular. During the Hongwu period of the Ming Dynasty, the houses on each street in Hangzhou planted Ilex chinensis to bring good luck.

Planting Ilex chinensis in cemeteries is a common practice. Li Zunkue passed by the ruined Shihu Southern Song Dynasty palace, and the line "Six Mausoleums, Wind and Rain, One Ilex chinensis" was widely recited by scholars.

Acknowledgement Since the publication of Yimei's Essays, they have been popular for a while. Now, the sequel has been published again. Yesterday, I received a complimentary copy from the Zhongfu Bookstore on Xiafei Road in this port. The content is richer than the first collection, and the beauty and elegance of the writing are truly extraordinary (priced at one yuan, special price 60%). I would like to express my gratitude and introduce it at the same time.

Swap Advance Short Position Paid Seven Yuan or So 251

The gold market was calm yesterday, the last day of February trading. Both buyers and sellers adopted a wait-and-see attitude. Although there were fluctuations depending on the swap spread throughout the day, transactions were dull and the situation was stagnant. In the early morning, overseas silver market saw British rise and American flat. The forward silver price rose and fell slightly. Exchange rates also plummeted. Grain 264

Rumors of Fixed Prices for Foreign Wheat Approach, Flour and Wheat Market Difficult to Break Free from Sluggishness

After the New Year opening of the flour market, the markets for various months have again shown signs of sluggishness and weakness. The quoted prices for foreign wheat in Chicago and Canada have fallen by about 4.5 dimes or so. When the market opened, due to the continued decline in foreign wheat prices and the approaching settlement date, many outside speculators sold off their holdings, resulting in an unstable opening and a drop of nearly 1 cent. Later, as inflows and outflows balanced, prices fluctuated. By the afternoon opening, the current month's market was sluggish due to weak actual sales, while distant months were rumored to have continued offers of foreign wheat. Although no transactions occurred, prices were close to market sentiment. As a result, the near-term market fell due to speculator sell-offs, while the distant-term market was weakened by the foreign wheat situation. The situation is likely to remain uncertain. As a result, the current month fell by 2 cents the day before, February fell by 2.5 cents, March fell by 2.75 cents, and April to June fell by 2.25 cents.

After the wheat market opened in the morning, the markets for various months showed signs of flatness and weakness. Quoted prices for foreign wheat were consistently about 4.5 dimes lower, resulting in a gloomy sentiment. The current month was stable due to a lack of selling, while distant months were more active, falling by 22 cents. By the afternoon opening, the flour market loosened, and the continuous hedging of foreign wheat weakened sentiment again, with near and distant months falling by 23 cents. Given the current situation, as the end of the year approaches, the market may inevitably experience fluctuations due to monetary conditions. As a result, the current month was down 4 dimes, February was down 7 dimes, and March and April were down 6 cents. The spot wheat market is declining steadily, factories are rejecting offers, and the entire market is closed.

Chicago wheat prices are extremely depressed due to the lack of improvement in Canadian wheat exports. The reflection in the Chicago market is the continued selling of long positions, causing the market to weaken again. Visible supplies this week are estimated to decrease by 3,072,000 bushels.

As a result, the market is quiet. Yesterday, Sassoon Foreign Firm needed 400 tons of immediate delivery cargo, and the market opened at 9.80 yuan. The situation remained mediocre. Spot transactions were limited to inquiries from the Dongyang group, and the market remained normal. Yesterday, 500 bags of Haozhou sesame were offered at prices of 7.35 and 7.20 yuan. 300 bags of Shashi sesame were priced at 7.49 yuan, and 230 bags of Guide sesame were priced at 7.20 yuan. Soybean sales are gradually declining, and the market is quite flat and sluggish.

Sugar Market 268

Another 2,000 Bags of Guangdong Coarse White Sugar Arrive

Sluggish Sales Market

Yesterday, the sugar market trend stabilized, mainly because sales slightly decreased. The guild's clearing price for Grade 24 coarse white sugar was 18.90 yuan for spot goods and 19 yuan for warehouse goods, with few transactions. Transshipment goods and Dutch red sugar were not traded. Taikoo sugar and local refined white sugar prices remained unchanged. The market saw the Chaozhou group offer 100 bags of original Binhuaqing at a price of 14 yuan and Chaoqing (various grades) offered 100+ bags at prices of 11 to 10.20 yuan, with no fluctuations. It is said that Beihai Pianqing was offered at 10.5 yuan, but the trading firm did not make a counteroffer due to the high price. The first batch of domestically produced Guangdong coarse white sugar, amounting to 800 bags, has arrived, and another 2,000 bags in the recent second batch have also arrived. It is expected that trading can commence within a day.

Jinshan Round Twigs in Zhabei Wholesale Market Rebound by 2-3 Yuan 269

Previously, due to sluggish sales of Jinshan round twigs, most of the goods from provincial groups had been released. As a result, ordinary goods had fallen to around 28 yuan. However, Hong Kong firms, considering the offered price to be too low, refused to sell except for a small amount of trading. Since entering the present period, sales from Jiangxi, Hunan, and Jin

Lanxi and other groups have been very active, and prices have turned around. In addition, trading firms with low inventories are also engaging in purchases. As a result, the market price has gradually rebounded by 2-3 yuan. According to industry insiders, it is predicted that the first market after the year-end closing will see high-grade round twigs priced above 40 yuan, as the total inventory in the Shanghai market is only about 20,000 boxes, and half of it is still being held by firms.

Abundant Arrival of Hardware Society Iron, Prices Decline 270

There have been many recent arrivals of Society Iron, so there is an exceptionally large amount circulating on the market. However, the standard grade is experiencing sluggish sales due to the abundant supply, resulting in very low offered prices. It is estimated to be 28.25 yuan per box, a decrease of 0.25 yuan compared to the previous price. It is said that the arrival of inferior goods is excessive, and the future market行情 may still face further declines.

Free Talk

The Demise of the Mountain Man Literature in Late Ming Dynasty 286

— Zai Qing

The flourishing of mountain men and celebrities mostly happens during times of societal decline. During these times, a segment of the intellectual class feels distressed about the current situation, but they don’t have the courage to be moths drawn to a flame, and they don’t want to bear the title of (coward) on the surface. So, becoming mountain men and celebrities becomes the way out for these people. The idea is that the uninhibited and highly recluse mountain men and celebrities are naturally meant to be (masters of mountains and waters), and they don't care about the (human world). Due to the influence of the declining era and the helpless mood of the surviving subjects, this trend will continue to exist in the early stages of each dynasty. Zheng Banqiao's family letters say (the streets are full of celebrities), which is obviously the result of this.

The reason why mountain men and celebrities were as numerous as (mosquitoes) in the late Ming and early Qing dynasties lies here. Mr. Tang Si once quoted Jiang Qiaosheng's poem scolding Chen Meigong, saying that Meigong (decorated the mountains and forests with a grand facade, and was a minor literary figure who flattered elegance. He had no intention of taking shortcuts to Zhongnan Mountain, but he exaggerated the false reputation of a recluse, and filled his works with borrowed knowledge, while his pursuits were to amass wealth and enjoy sensual pleasures. He was like a crane flying between the clouds, flying to and from the prime minister's office.) This poem is indeed a very harsh exposure of the true ugly state of mountain men and celebrities. Zhang Zongzi also mentioned Chen Meigong in his (self-written epitaph). When Zongzi was sixteen years old, his grandfather took him to Wulin to play, and he met Meigong. Meigong was a tourist in Qiantang at this time. He gave Zongzi a (couplet) to answer, saying (Taibai rides a whale, fishing for the night moon by the Caishi River). Zongzi immediately responded with the scene: (Meigong rides a deer, begging for favors in Qiantang County.) Meigong couldn't express his bitterness, so he had to praise him a lot. Therefore, in (inopportune) times, on one hand, there is the prosperity of mountain men and celebrities, and on the other hand, there is the intensification of opposition to mountain men and celebrities. Taking the late Ming Dynasty as an example, Chen Meigong suffered like this, and others were attacked in the same way. Wang Baigu was the authority of famous mountain men and celebrities in the Southeast, and Zhang Fengyi was the first to write (Song of the Mountain Man) to scold him. This song initially directly named Baigu, but after opposition from friends, it was changed to Shen Jiazhe, and as a result of further opposition, the name of the mountain man was not mentioned at all. Not long after, I saw a notebook with a poem satirizing Baigu, using the bayberry fruit to describe the skin disease on his body. Yuan Shigong's decadent stage in the capital, from his words (others laugh at me for being confused), can also be seen the attitude of the opponents at that time. Although Jiang Jinzhi has a (hypothetical statement that the speaker speaks for himself, and the person concerned does what he should do, so how can idle talk lead to the downfall of the country. But Jin people's talk should take transcendence and purity as its purpose, saying that it can ruin the country is wrong, saying that it cannot save the customs of the country, even if Wang Yifu and other gentlemen are resurrected, they cannot explain it. Therefore, what is valued in talk is its ability to save customs) this more progressive and compromising explanation, it could not stop the anti-mountain man and celebrity movement at that time.

Xue Gang has a (Letter of Resignation to Friends Claiming to be Mountain Men) which exposes the ugly state of mountain men to a great extent. He said, (The title of mountain man is not found in ancient times, but there were such people; it is prevalent today, but there is little reality; people with aspirations are ashamed of this name.) He lists ten ugly states of mountain men: (First, their bodies are not clothed in formal attire, their homes are humble and crude, they find it difficult to get close to prominent figures, so they steal beautiful names, thinking of mingling with officials and scholars, in order to gain favor. Second, after stealing a beautiful name, they immediately forget their true nature. Even if they have not mastered the rules of writing, they also discuss poetry and literature. If you ask them about their learning, they are at a loss for words. Third, they have a meager talent, and they mingle with honored guests. At moonlit feasts and flower banquets, they advance and retreat together, bowing and yielding and acting pretentiously, without any doubt. Fourth, as soon as they hear of a hospitable person, they try every means to make friends. They regard prominent people as rare commodities. As soon as they have the chance to socialize, they slander their introducers. Fifth, they observe their joy and anger, and cater to them in every possible way. They get their intentions and follow them closely, trying to win praise. Sixth, they meet by chance and immediately visit their homes. They carry name cards and deliver them everywhere, feeling that the day is not enough. They are respectful and humble, and follow others' lead from the beginning. Seventh, regardless of age, they always sign their name cards as younger, and regardless of the depth of their relationship, they all claim to be close friends. They are complacent when they boast to others about how widespread their connections are. Eighth, after claiming to be mountain men, they have no rustic charm at all. They wear light clothes and ride fat horses, live in spacious houses and eat luxurious food, and gallop through the capital to show off their success. Ninth, they greedily seek favor and their tongues can lick. If they slightly offend my feelings, they often scold people at the table. They ask the prominent person to exempt them from seeing guests at their gate. Tenth, and the worst of all, they have close and secretive friendships, and secretly pry into hidden details. Their minds are full of schemes, which are impossible to fathom. They hold people's shortcomings and use them to make themselves feel better.) Finally, he also said, (The shame is greatest for a mountain man), and changed (mountain man) to (mountain mix). There is probably no more ugly and blatant exposure of (mountain men) than this.

Zheng Chaozong once commented on this letter, saying: (Every time I travel in the mountains, I don't meet a single one. They walk arm in arm on thoroughfares and in mansions. I secretly wonder where the two words "mountain man" are attached. This article is enough to speak out for the mountains). The first four words can be described as extremely humorous. Not only that, Zhu Quanzai also once (spoke of celebrities). However, in his view, he was not fundamentally opposed to (celebrities), but rather opposed to (fake celebrities.) As for (fake celebrities), he quoted Wang Xiaobo's words, (A celebrity does not necessarily need to be a genius, but if he can often drink wine without doing anything and read the "Li Sao" thoroughly, he can be called a celebrity), as an explanation. He also quoted Wang Taiwei's dialogue with Meizi, (Wang Taiwei asked Meizi, "Your uncle is a celebrity, why don't you recommend him?" Meizi said, ("What is a celebrity? He utters nonsense all day long.") and added a footnote: (In order to socialize, a celebrity must utter nonsense all day long, so how can one say that uttering nonsense all day long is not a celebrity?) That is the true color of a celebrity. Li Zhuowu was also a person who opposed mountain men and celebrities, and his attitude was even more intense. In a letter to Jiao Ruohou, he wrote: (From this point of view, today's so-called sages are the same as today's so-called mountain men, but they differ in luck. If they are lucky enough to be able to write poetry, they call themselves mountain men; if they are unlucky and cannot write poetry, they reject the title of mountain man and use the name of sage. If they are lucky enough to be able to speak of innate knowledge, they call themselves sages; if they are unlucky and cannot speak of innate knowledge, they reject the title of sage and call themselves mountain men. They turn around and deceive the world to gain profit, called mountain men, but their hearts are the same as merchants, talking about morality, but their ambitions are to steal and cheat.) (Stripping off ten layers of the face) (Wei Yong's commentary on Xue Gang's words) is the most appropriate footnote to this article. Zhuowu's entire life existed in struggle. His book (Burning Book) is simply a history of ideological struggle, which is fully expressed in this short chapter of opposing mountain men and celebrities.

At that time, there were certainly more documents against mountain men and celebrities than just these. But just looking at these, we can also know that when mountain men and celebrities were most active, the front line against mountain men and celebrities was also developing. This anti-celebrity movement continued for a long time. In Banqiao's family letters, you can see chapters scolding mountain men and celebrities in the collection of letters from the early Qing Dynasty as well. Although some of these people who opposed mountain men and celebrities themselves failed to completely get rid of the habits of mountain men and celebrities and change, their dissatisfaction and hatred are very clear. Although the times are different now, new mountain men flourish due to objective circumstances, and new celebrities wave their banners, which is clearly visible to everyone. Some are even like (my family's doctor), not satisfied with calling themselves that, but also bring out (historical evidence), claiming that (it has existed since ancient times), but what (has existed since ancient times) is not only the camp of mountain men and celebrities, but also the group that opposes mountain men and celebrities. The ancients can be talked about, and ancient texts can also be talked about, but the question is whether it should be objective. Using dead people as your own shield is something that even the gentlemen of the late Ming Dynasty would know is wrong if they were alive today.

Discerning Words and Discerning Phrases (5) 287

— Cao Juren

Guest: According to what you said, the use of vague and general words is still the fault of the old literati, and modern youth cannot be blamed. Now (don't talk about success, don't blame the past), all the past is like yesterday's death, from now on, to make the language level of modern youth particularly improved, is there any positive proposal?

Host: Yes, yes, yes! When Zhang Shizhao was running the Jiayin Magazine and advocating logical literature, he had a very good proposal. He said: (Do not write in the article if the form is not satisfactory; do not put the word in the sentence if its use is not clear; strive to avoid vagueness, and be incisive. Clearly see the artistic conception in the writing, and distinguish between right and wrong; like watching fish swimming in a stream, you can see the bottom clearly; like examining a spider on the spiderweb, the silk is clearly divided; this is almost it. I have the ambition to do this, but I dare not say I have achieved it! However, there are words that cannot be left out in the article, and the determination of meaning and the use of words must follow the laws set down in the mind, and should not be easily slipped over; if suddenly questioned, it is very rare that the meaning is there but the reason cannot be spoken.) (On Literature) Later, Hu Shi advocated the literary revolution, and also said: (Today's scholars, if they remember a few literary clichés in their minds, they call themselves poets. Their poems and essays are full of clichés and worn-out tunes. The bad result is that many poems and essays that are seemingly right but actually wrong, seemingly similar but actually not, are produced in the country... What I mean by going to clichés and worn-out tunes is that everyone should use their own eyes and ears to describe and depict the things they have seen and experienced in person; only seek to not lose the truth, only seek to be able to achieve the purpose of expressing things and writing intentions, that is the effort.) (Preliminary Proposals for Literary Improvement) We must open up a living path for modern youth, (everything in the future is like being born today), only by completely separating youth from the old literati, and not letting youth be infected with those old germs. On the one hand, we should do basic work in terms of rhetoric and sentence-making: compile some simple and accurate dictionaries for young people, (not as messy as the Ciyuan) so that young people can easily look them up, sort out perfect grammar and rhetoric books for young people, so that young people have rules to follow; make a perfect word differentiation book for young people, (word differentiation is definitely not word differentiation) put the same types of words together so that they can be used flexibly, annotate words that look similar so that they can dispel doubts; select a living anthology for young people, (not dead articles like Han Yu, Liu Zongyuan, Ouyang Xiu, and Su Shi) so that they can have good role models. If people who care about language work hard to do this, in ten or twenty years, the results will be visible!

Guest: Are there people doing this part of the positive work?

Host: Who are we waiting for to do it? You and I are both Chinese teachers above the intermediate level, shouldn't we work harder? (End)

About (Autobiography) 288

— Wei Zhongtian

I have always loved to read autobiographies or books of the autobiographical type. I have read Rousseau's Confessions, Lenin's biography, Mussolini's and Hitler's autobiographies, as well as Hu Shi's Forty Years of Self-Narrative, Shen Congwen's, and Record of Ding Ling. Reading other people's autobiographies allows you to understand their lives, personalities, hobbies, and worldviews in great detail. Therefore, I really like reading this kind of book. A good autobiography is one that can truthfully write out the experiences of one's past life without any concealment, such as Rousseau's Confessions. However, some people are not like that. They want to show off by writing an autobiography, writing themselves as a genius, a very capable person. They hide all the shameful experiences and foolish behaviors. I have seen some people's autobiographies in a certain magazine before, and they really gave me a headache!

Recently, I borrowed a copy of Duncan's autobiography from a friend, and I felt very satisfied after reading it. This is also a good book. She doesn't brag or hide her shortcomings, but writes boldly. There are many parts that are really touching, making people shed tears of sympathy. She writes about the pain of struggling on the line of starvation when she and her mother flowed from the countryside to the city, and the lack of travel expenses when she took a cattle boat from New York to London, being rejected by the hotel owner and spending three days and three nights on the street, and then using deception to stay in a very luxurious hotel. These emotional descriptions are extremely moving, so I say this is a good book.

I advocate that everyone can write an autobiography. Autobiographies don't necessarily have to be written well by celebrities, scholars, or artists. In fact, if they can write truthfully and boldly, a rickshaw puller, a beggar, an actor, a prostitute, a smoker, or a street singer might write even more moving stories. It's just a pity that they don't have the skills to use words and cannot write it out, so all the touching stories and depraved stories are buried in their own hearts. For example, my father, he was a farmer and a small businessman. He lost his grandfather when he was seven or eight years old, and lived and grew up in various forms of bullying and pain until he was able to be a peddler himself. He didn't know how much wind and frost he had endured and how much hunger he had suffered. He told me that for a long period of time, he and his grandmother ate vegetable leaves, sweet potatoes, and tears every day. In this situation, there was absolutely no opportunity for education. In his middle age, he also served as a brave soldier on the front line in a clan fight, holding a fire cannon, killing people, and seeing dozens of heads hung high on tree trunks. Under the tree trunks, a group of people gathered, drinking, singing, and gloriously looking at those spoils of war! In his own village, he watched people's eyes being gouged out, ears being cut off... He had seen too much of the inhuman acts of strong families bullying weak families, and he felt it was too common. I believe that if my father could write an autobiography, it would definitely be very moving. It's a pity that he can't write it either. Maybe one day I'll write it for him, but of course, other people's feelings can't compare to his own.

Also, I have a girlfriend who is often in love affairs. In five years, she has loved more than a dozen people, including university professors, college students, writers, and officials... These kinds of people, however, the small storms in the river of love cannot discourage her. To this day, she still has that courage, and she is still as young and beautiful as ever. She has used coats that cost three or four hundred yuan, silk stockings that cost twenty yuan a pair, and gloves that cost twenty-eight yuan a pair, but when storms occurred in the river of love, she only ate fried dough sticks and flatbread for a living, wore outdated clothes, and even borrowed ten or twenty cents from people. I believe that if she wrote an autobiography, it would also be very impressive. So I think that writing an autobiography doesn't necessarily have to be done by celebrities, scholars, or artists. Anyone can write it, as long as his or her life is unique, twisted, and extraordinary, it is enough to write an autobiography.

Chinese and Western Clothing 289

— TK

The Human World (1) 290

— Li Huiying

(Friend, why can't we get there no matter how far we walk, what's going on? Moreover, we're always walking on dark roads, where are you trying to lead me)?

I couldn't bear it any longer, and I finally said it out, questioning my friend who was walking with me: My friend, you originally said you were going to lead me to open up the social customs, but in Harbin, does opening up the social customs really mean going to dark places? What kind of social customs are we trying to open up?

He was a graduate of a Shanghai sports school, and had been an elementary school physical education teacher in Harbin for six years. Our separation was also exactly six years. I was really surprised to be able to meet him in Harbin this time. For six years, due to the interruption of communication, my memory had long forgotten my friend's figure and face. The two of us met in Daoli Garden. He was wearing a black suit that was quite unsuitable for summer. Not to mention that there were quite a few wrinkles on the suit, which didn't look very good, but it was also stained with some oil stains. He was holding a thin stick that was peeling paint and black all over in his right hand, and wearing a faded straw hat on his head. He was standing in front of the park cinema, staring intently at the advertisement for the Burning of the Red Lotus Temple. I first saw his back, but it immediately made me think of Cao Baohua, who was known among his fellow villagers for being unkempt six years ago. Sure enough, my guess was correct. When I walked up to him and recognized him, he also recognized me at the same time. He opened his mouth before me and said:

(Haven't left yet? Are we in the human world? Is it really you who came back? Sigh!...)

He sighed and couldn't continue speaking, but I could tell that his words were full of infinite sadness and emotion. I guessed that he thought it was a mistake for me to come back this time.

I didn't answer his words immediately, but pulled him to the ice cream parlor next door, sat down, and then talked to him about our lives in the past six years.

After that, we came and went very often, spending at least two or three hours together every day.

One night, I went to his house again. As soon as I entered the door, he said impatiently:

(Wei Hang, tonight I'll take you to open up the social customs.)

I was very happy about this, so I asked excitedly:

(That's great, but where are we going)?

(You don't need to ask, you'll know when we get there.)

But his words couldn't satisfy me. I still asked:

(Are we going to a brothel)?

He shook his head.

(Then, are we going to a small restaurant with female waitresses)?

From my friend's second shake of his head, it proved that I was wrong again. I pretended to be angry and said loudly:

(I guess there's probably no roulette in Harbin, or maybe it's an opium den)!

(Don't ask, you'll know in a while.)

After a while, I walked with him on the road, following him to find a place to open up the social customs.

The Voice of the Telegraph

Understanding Telegraphs 291

— Lv Bing

If you want to make use of things, you must first have a full understanding of them. A full understanding, in layman's terms, means knowing the threshold. If you don't understand the threshold well, you will only have a superficial understanding, so how can you make full use of it?

Using the telegraph to obtain the speed of communication between the two parties is well known to ordinary people. But how fast is the telegraph exactly? And how to write and send it? How can the telegraph's efficiency be fully realized, and how can the sender reduce its expenses? This is of great value for those who use the telegraph to study. Therefore, simply knowing the convenience of the telegraph does not necessarily mean that you really understand the telegraph. You must understand the threshold of sending telegraphs before you can.

In the past, people in society often did not study how to send telegrams economically and cost-effectively. They were also mostly unaware of the transmission routes of the bureaus and stations. However, in recent years, the situation has changed greatly. Those who send telegrams have made a lot of progress in understanding the threshold. They know exactly how long it will take for a telegram sent to a certain place to arrive, and how long it will take to get a reply. Occasionally, if there is a line blockage or congestion, which causes a slight delay, they often call to ask for the number. Therefore, the handling of telegraph business in today's bureaus and stations is very different from the past. This is because the reporter lives in Tianjin and the business personnel told me about it, which is indeed a matter of experience.

In fact, this phenomenon shows the progress of society's understanding of the telegraph, and it is also what the bureau and station personnel expect. In recent years, the Ministry of Communications has spared no effort in improving business, such as increasing the transmission speed and verifying the accuracy of telegrams. Since the implementation, the results have been remarkable. The purpose is nothing more than to make everyone know that the telegraph is indeed fast and accurate, in order to obtain the development of business and seek the convenience of social communication. If the people of the country cannot fully understand the telegraph, there will be many obstacles in the future of the business. Now that the threshold is well understood, and the public also knows the situation of the bureaus and stations handling business, in the future, the use of telegraphs will become more and more popular. The progress of all businesses often depends on the spur of all parties, and the telegraph is no exception.

Talking to Various Shipping Companies about the Unpaid Telegraph Fees for Ships 292

— Fen

Ship telegraphs are divided into two categories: incoming and outgoing. Some are transmitted through domestic coastal radio stations, and some are transmitted through foreign coastal radio stations. Incoming telegrams are sent by ships to coastal radio stations for delivery, or sent by ships to coastal radio stations for forwarding to various local bureaus for delivery. Outgoing telegrams are sent directly by coastal radio stations to ships, or sent by local bureaus to coastal radio stations for forwarding to ships. When sending telegrams to ships, the coastal radio stations or local bureaus can collect all the fees that should be paid at the time. Telegrams sent by ships to land cannot be paid at the time because they are being sent while sailing at sea. They can only be temporarily recorded and settled later by the relevant telecommunications authorities with the company to which the ship belongs. The accounts for telegrams sent through domestic coastal radio stations are settled by the Ministry of Communications every quarter (three months). The Ministry of Communications sends a statement of incoming and outgoing telegrams to each shipping company for verification and payment. Those transmitted through foreign coastal radio stations are sent by the telecommunications authorities of the countries concerned to the Ministry of Communications for collection from the shipping companies. According to the International Radio Telegraph Regulations, shipping companies must pay the fees within six weeks of receiving the statement. If there are any discrepancies, they must request correction within six months of receiving the statement, otherwise it will be considered as an acknowledgment. If the fees are not paid after six months, interest will be charged at 6% per annum. Therefore, when foreign telegraph bureaus or foreign ships send telegrams through our country's coastal radio stations and owe fees to the Ministry of Communications, the Ministry of Communications receives the money on time when it collects the money from the telecommunications authorities of various countries every quarter. This shows that the governments and merchants of various countries attach great importance to credit and obey international regulations. The speed of their handling is just a matter of course. However, this is not the case in our country. It is said that when our country's shipping companies receive the wireless telegraph statements issued by the Ministry of Communications, most of them pay the fees according to regulations, but there are also many who owe part or all of the fees. Some of them have been in arrears for several years, and the amount of arrears ranges from several hundred to several thousand yuan. Although the Ministry of Communications has repeatedly urged them to pay, they have not paid. This account includes those entrusted by foreign telecommunications authorities to the Ministry of Communications for collection. These authorities do not understand the reason why Chinese shipping companies do not pay, and have repeatedly urged the Ministry of Communications to pay in strict terms. The Ministry of Communications is in a difficult position to answer. This kind of arrears is not a small matter in terms of international credit, so I will explain it in detail as follows:

(1) As mentioned above, it is necessary to temporarily record the telegrams sent by ships due to the circumstances. However, some of the telegrams sent by ships are sent by the ships themselves, and some are sent by passengers. The fees for those sent by passengers have already been collected by the ships. The shipping companies only need to deduct the ship fees that they should get, and the remaining fees are all collected on behalf of the passengers. The companies must pay the fees according to regulations. At present, the shipping companies not only fail to pay the fees that they owe themselves, but also drag on the fees collected on behalf of the passengers. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications has great difficulties in accounting.

(2) When the Ministry of Communications collects fees from shipping companies, the companies often fail to pay on time. The reasons they give are either that the business is not prosperous and the economy is difficult, or that the accounts do not match and need to be checked. If the company's business is not prosperous, it is an internal problem, so let's put it aside for the time being. As for the mismatch of accounts, the company can order the ships under its jurisdiction to check the telegram copies in detail, or directly request a review from the Ministry of Communications. Moreover, each quarterly account is only ten to several hundred yuan. If it can be paid quarterly, the burden is not too heavy. In addition, there are still the fees collected on behalf of passengers in a quarterly account. The fees that the company itself should pay are only a small part of it, which is even smaller. However, the company repeatedly delays payment, day after day, so the arrears become more and more, and it is impossible to pay them. It is not a good idea for the company.

(3) The persons in charge of the company, such as directors and managers, are all important figures in society. They are afraid that they will not have time to maintain their credit, so there is no reason to intentionally delay payment. Perhaps some employees in the company (such as accountants or bookkeepers) think that this kind of account is no different from the accounts of ordinary merchants, and they can owe it if they want to. They don't know that part of this account is the fees owed to foreign telecommunications authorities. These authorities have already deducted it from the accounts between them and the Ministry of Communications. If the company owes it for a long time, the Ministry of Communications will not be able to make up for it. The company's responsible authorities should inform the internal employees in detail so that these arrears can be settled as soon as possible.

It is said that the Ministry of Communications believes that this kind of account cannot be suspended for a long time for the sake of international credit, and will formulate measures to severely crack down on it. The company's authorities are all enlightened people and will surely be able to appreciate the government's difficulties and pay off the debt as soon as possible.

International Radio Station Over the Past Year (Continued) 293

— Zhang Chenghu

(B) Business Development

The expansion of the international radio station's facilities is as described above. Business operations should also follow suit, so that all equipment can be fully utilized and business can prosper. Here are the new business items undertaken by the station in the past year:

Opening of New Lines 丨 Before the 23rd year, the international radio station successively opened communication lines to Hong Kong, Manila, Java, Saigon, San Francisco, Berlin, Paris, Geneva, and Moscow. However, due to equipment limitations, it was inconvenient to add more. In February of the 23rd year, the Marconi machine was installed, and a direct line to London was opened. Thus, this central metropolis of world politics and economy also became a place closely connected with the international station day and night. Later, the Ministry of Communications, considering the large number of Japanese expatriates in China and the frequent telegraphic communications, which relied on submarine cables and resulted in the loss of rights, deeply regretted this. It negotiated with the Japanese government and opened a line to Tokyo on June 1st. By then, famous cities and towns in the East and West could communicate through the international radio station in an instant.

Dedicated Line for Receiving and Sending Telegrams 丨 For the convenience of large banks and businesses in Shanghai with a high volume of telegrams, the international radio station rented dedicated lines from the Shanghai Telephone Company, directly connecting these businesses to the station's telegraph room. Telephones or teletype machines were installed at both ends for exchanging telegrams. This service also began on a trial basis in the 23rd year. As more and more businesses in the finance and stock industries began to use it, the station set up a dedicated line exchange and assigned dedicated personnel to manage it day and night to facilitate operations. If businesses wished to send personnel to the station to receive and send telegrams, they could rent soundproof rooms from the station. The structure of these rooms allowed for sound isolation, and a dedicated telephone line connected directly to the business. When personnel stationed at the station contacted their companies by telephone, there was no risk of revealing commercial secrets.

Increasing Telegram Delivery Efficiency 丨 For telegrams arriving from various locations, except for those using dedicated lines, the international station delivered them to the recipients by messengers riding bicycles. To improve delivery efficiency, more than 20 new messengers were hired successively last year to ensure telegrams were delivered as soon as they arrived. Each messenger was required to deliver only one telegram per trip to avoid delays. Shanghai was divided into several zones, with specified delivery times for each zone. Messengers were strictly required to deliver within the time limit, with penalties for delays and rewards for timely delivery. Those who could find ways to deliver telegrams to unclear addresses were also rewarded. Therefore, all messengers strived to deliver quickly.

Reducing Telegram Copying Errors 丨 While speed is essential for telegrams, accuracy is even more important. Moreover, the international radio station handles a lot of commercial intelligence in its transmitted and received telegrams, and a single error can lead to significant liabilities. To enhance the station's reputation, every effort was made to avoid errors. In October of the 23rd year, the Ministry of Communications approved the recruitment of 30 telegram clerks to be trained as full-time proofreaders. All incoming and outgoing telegrams were proofread immediately after receipt or dispatch. If any errors were found, the parties concerned would be notified immediately for correction without waiting for inquiries, to ensure the public's absolute trust in the reliability of the international radio station.

Business Inspection 丨 The Ministry of Communications strives to satisfy users of telegram services. Therefore, it seeks detailed information through surveys and inquiries. It ordered all bureaus and stations across the country to establish business inspectors to specifically inquire about users' opinions on the bureaus and stations. Special attention was paid to international telegrams handled by the international radio station. Any deficiencies in operations and areas needing improvement or reform could be reported to the inspectors. The station would humbly adopt and strive to improve these suggestions.

Distribution of Booklets 丨 Since the 23rd year, the international radio station has been publishing a booklet issued monthly, in both Chinese and English, containing information about the international radio station and basic knowledge of international telegrams for users' reference. The booklet is mailed to major businesses in Shanghai and other cities on a regular basis. If any are missed, they can be requested from the station, and will be sent immediately free of charge.

Creation of Delayed News Telegrams 丨 According to the regulations attached to the International Telegraph Convention, news telegrams should be dispatched earlier than ordinary telegrams, while delayed telegrams are the opposite. However, the charge for news telegrams is only 20% to 25% of the ordinary rate, as news telegrams often contain many words and are given special treatment to facilitate the news industry. However, sometimes the news is not very important, and transmission can be slightly delayed. If charged at the news telegram rate, it would still be too expensive, or even prohibitive. To promote international news, the Ministry of Communications created a type of delayed news telegram with a lower rate than news telegrams, and the dispatch procedure is after ordinary telegrams but before delayed telegrams. Currently, agreements have been reached only with the United States and Canada, and it was implemented in May of last year. Negotiations are still ongoing with other countries.

The above points are the major new facilities in business over the past year. Other minor matters, such as expanding the locations reachable by the Japan line, handling the receipt and dispatch of telegrams by city telephones, establishing business inquiry offices, and organizing registration, are not detailed. More important matters that are still in progress are as follows:

Wireless Telephone Communication 丨 The Ministry of Communications plans to add wireless telephone equipment to the international radio station, as mentioned earlier. In the spring and summer of last year, the station used the Marconi machine's broadcast equipment to conduct preliminary telephone experiments. The locations tested included London, Berlin, San Francisco, Geneva, and Manila. Liu Chongjie, the Chinese ambassador to Germany, Hu Shize, the ambassador to Switzerland, Mr. and Mrs. Cunningham, the American consul-general in Shanghai, and prominent Shanghai figures such as Liu Hongsheng and Huang Jiangquan, participated in the conversations and concluded that it was possible to open commercial services. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications is currently negotiating communication methods with various countries.

China-Italy Communication 丨 Rome, the capital of Italy, is one of the political centers of Europe and has repeatedly requested communication with China last year. Joint experiments were conducted, but initially, the Italian side's transmission was weak and not smooth. After repeated improvements, it has become perfect. Once the contract is signed, official communication can begin.

Special Personnel to Pick Up Telegrams 丨 Since the Ministry of Communications implemented postal and telecommunications cooperation, post offices in Shanghai have been collecting international wireless telegrams on behalf of the station. Senders can submit telegrams at their nearest post office, saving the trouble of long journeys. However, Shanghai's urban area is vast, and sometimes it is still inconvenient. Therefore, people use telephones to notify the international radio station to send personnel to pick up telegrams. This was previously done by messengers, but messengers could not calculate fees or collect money, so it was limited to account-holding businesses. To make it more accessible, it is planned to assign several special personnel to handle it. The international radio station will purchase several motorized vehicles. Upon receiving a telephone call, they will immediately drive to pick up the telegram and return to the station to dispatch it, similar to telephone shopping in stores. Customers can communicate with foreign countries at any time without leaving their homes.

(C) Statistical Summary

The international radio station has made progress in both construction and business over the past year, sparing no effort. Readers are eager to know the effects of this. Here is a summary of statistics to show a glimpse of the results.

Business Status 丨 The international radio station transmitted and received 50,000 telegrams per month last year, totaling 700,000 words, which is a significant increase compared to previous years. Revenue has also increased accordingly. Here is a simple chart showing the total number of words, telegrams, and revenue in silver dollars over the years, to show the growth.

Telegram Transmission Speed 丨 For international telegrams, except for those using dedicated lines, ordinary senders bring their telegrams to the general receiving and dispatching office of the international radio station in the Sassoon House on Renji Road, where a telegram clerk calculates the number of words and the fee, prints the dispatch time, and sends the telegram to the telegraph room via pneumatic tube. The registering clerk logs the number, indicates the route, and passes it to the dispatch operator for transmission. This process takes about 45 seconds. The automatic high-speed machine is used for transmission, and the speed can reach 300 to 400 words per minute. However, due to differences in equipment and methods at the receiving stations, the transmission speed varies from location to location, as shown in the table below.

Location　　Words sent and received per minute (Average 5 letters per word)　Location　　Words sent and received per minute (Average 5 letters per word)

San Francisco　160　　　　　　　　　　London　　350

Berlin　　300　　　　　　　　　　Paris　200

Geneva　150　　　　　　　　　　Tokyo　　150

Moscow　80　　　　　　　　　　　Manila　150

Batavia　120　　　　　　　　　　Hong Kong　　100

Saigon　80

The handling procedure for telegrams from abroad is the opposite of the above. Incoming telegrams are recorded by an automatic waveform machine, and the speed is about the same as shown in the previous table. After the receiving operator copies it using a typewriter, it is sent to the registering clerk via a belt conveyor for registration, and then it is assigned to the dispatcher, who prepares an envelope. Then, it is sent to the dispatch room via a pneumatic tube, and the messenger immediately sets off by bicycle. This process takes about one minute and twenty seconds. The delivery time for the messenger depends on the distance, and there are specified time limits for all locations in Shanghai. Messengers are not allowed to linger on the way. The time limit table is lengthy and not recorded.

Error Records 丨 The number of errors increases and decreases depending on the tightness of management and fluctuates with business conditions. Although the actual number of errors last year was higher than the previous year, it decreased compared to previous years when calculated as a percentage of the total number of words sent and received, as shown in the table below:

The international radio station has achieved these results in the four years since its establishment. This is due to the support and encouragement from the central government and the efforts of the Ministry of Communications. However, without the love of our national people for state-owned enterprises and the promotion of reclaiming rights, these achievements would not have been possible. Thinking of the difficult beginnings, and looking forward to perfecting the future, we deeply hope that the communications authorities will further expand the existing rules so that business can improve and innovate day by day. Then, the future of China's telecommunications administration will be promising. (End)

Free Inquiry of Telegrams 295

— Qinghua

When this publication was founded, I wrote an article titled "(Notes on Inquiring About Telegrams)," which was published in the first few issues of this publication. Later, when the Ministry of Communications compiled and printed the booklet "(Summary of New Regulations on Saving Telegram Fees)," it also included this "(Notes on Inquiring About Telegrams)" with the aim of enabling readers to know how to inquire about telegrams and obtain full convenience. However, although 50,000 copies of this booklet were printed and distributed, it is estimated that fewer than 50,000 people actually received it, and even fewer people saw the "(Notes on Inquiring About Telegrams)" included in it! That's why I once heard someone say: "(I received a telegram one day, and there seemed to be a mistake in one of the words in the telegram. I didn't understand it, so I sent a telegram to ask my friend. Later, I received a reply telegram, and sure enough, the word was wrong. I asked the telegraph office to refund the fees for the two telegrams we sent back and forth for inquiry, but the telegraph office refused to refund them. They only refunded the fee for the wrong word, which made me extremely indignant because it was too unfair!)" When ordinary people hear this, they will definitely say that the telegraph office is wrong, but let me explain the regulations, and you will know that someone suffered a loss because he didn't understand the regulations and can't blame the telegraph office for refusing to refund the fees.

The telegraph office receives and sends thousands of telegrams a day, and even small offices receive dozens. Each telegram averages 20 words, so more than 100,000 words are sent and received every day, and at least a thousand words. It is inevitable to make mistakes in the hustle and bustle. It is reasonable to have one or two errors in 10,000 words. We can't say that the telegraph office staff is not doing their job. Since telegrams are inevitably prone to errors, the telegraph office has specially stipulated a remedy, that is, if the recipient of a telegram believes that there is a doubt about a word or number in the telegram, they can immediately inquire with the telegraph office. The telegraph office will immediately send an official telegram to the sending office for inquiry free of charge. After receiving the telegram, the sending office will check it against the original. If it is indeed a transmission error, it will immediately send a reply telegram to correct it (if it is not wrong, it will also send a reply notification). After receiving the reply telegram, the receiving office will immediately notify the recipient. With such an inquiry, neither the recipient nor the sender needs to spend any money, and the reply can be obtained earlier than inquiring by sending a telegram themselves. Because inquiring by sending a telegram requires the telegraph office to send the inquiry telegram to the original sender, and then wait for him to verify it before sending someone to send the reply telegram to the telegraph office for transmission. This back-and-forth trip takes at least an hour. If the telegraph office sends an official telegram to inquire, the official telegram can be checked and replied to immediately when it reaches the other telegraph office, saving the time of sending the telegram twice, and the official telegram is faster than commercial telegrams in transmission, so the reply is of course obtained faster. With these two advantages, why should we send our own telegrams to inquire?

After reading the above explanation, readers will know that someone suffered a loss because he didn't understand the regulations, not because the telegraph office was unreasonable! However, we can't just blame someone for not understanding the regulations, but also blame our colleagues in the telecommunications industry for lacking publicity, so even now there are several banks and companies that still don't know the method of inquiring about telegrams for free, resulting in frequent unpleasant incidents of requesting refunds. I hope that the business inspectors of major offices will pay special attention to this point, publicize and explain more to major businesses at any time, and give them the booklet on saving fees, so that they feel the thoughtfulness of the telegraph office's telegraphic service and increase their confidence in using telegrams!

Finally, I would like to tell readers: Inquiring about telegrams is not limited to doubts about the wording of the telegram. If there are missing words, errors in the place of origin, errors in the date of transmission, or other questions, you can always inquire by telephone or in person. The telegraph office will answer sincerely. If there is arrogance or failure to answer immediately, you can report it to the Ministry of Communications for investigation, and you will receive a satisfactory answer.

How to Utilize Telegrams 296

— Zhonghua

In the previous issues of this publication, there was an article by Mr. Qinghua called (The Small Threshold for Sending Telegrams), in which he explained in detail how to make sending telegrams profitable (cheap and good)! However, in addition to (cheap and good), it seems that we also need to study the convenience of (procurement). It turns out that there are many convenient ways to send telegrams, but our Chinese telegram-sending public has not fully utilized them, so I will talk about (how to utilize telegrams) to introduce them to readers. If you live in a place that only has a post office and no telegraph office, and you need to send a telegram to relatives and friends in a distant place, it is completely wrong if you think that you cannot send a telegram! You can use the same procedure, pay the same fees, and send a telegram at the post office. The post office will use the fastest method to send it to the nearest telegraph office for transmission. Conversely. If you want to send a telegram to a place that has no telegraph office but only a post office, the situation is the same; the telegraph office will send it to the nearest telegraph office to the destination for mailing. This method is commonly called (postal telegram).

Someone said: It is true that you can send postal telegrams in places with post offices but no telegraph offices, but what about places with no post offices or telegraph offices? This is easy to solve; the telegraph office will hire a temporary messenger to send it to you. The messenger's fee will be paid by the recipient or you can pay it in advance. However, add (special delivery) or an Express character before the recipient's name and address, which will be counted as one word for the fee. If you pay the express fee in advance, add an XP character before the recipient's name and address (meaning (express fee paid)), which will also be counted as one word for the fee. In telegraphic terminology, this method is called (special delivery telegram).

It has already been said above that there is absolutely no problem for two fixed places to send telegrams to each other. But suppose your friend is traveling in Europe and America or traveling in famous mountains and rivers in the country, and there is no fixed itinerary, you can still use (follow-up telegram) to communicate with him or her. What is called (follow-up telegram)? That is, the telegraph offices in various places automatically send it to the destination for you, that is, the telegraph office will find the recipient for you until it is found and delivered properly. You also need to add an FS character before the recipient's name and address for this type of telegram, which will be counted as one word for the fee. The sender only needs to pay the fee for a section of the itinerary in advance, and the rest will be collected from the recipient by the telegraph office.

There is also a type of (transferred telegram), which is similar to the above situation, that is, when the recipient cannot receive it due to other matters, a related person can request it to be transferred to a certain place without having to send another telegram. Although the fee still needs to be calculated, this allows the recipient to immediately know the ins and outs of the telegram, saving the tone of the middleman's narration, and the sender can also get a relatively quick reply.

The World of Telecommunications 297

— Reporter

Current Status of Telegrams in Turkey Turkey currently has 631 telegraph offices, with a total line length of 66,580 kilometers and a number of 14,804,516 telegrams, of which 13,987,516 are domestic telegrams, 400,000 are international outgoing telegrams, 410,000 are international incoming telegrams, and 7,000 are transit telegrams. The telegraph income is approximately 1,574,562 Turkish pounds. (One Turkish pound is approximately six US dollars.) There are a total of 5,470 employees, of which 4,780 are engaged in telegraph work.

Change of Name of Czech Telegraph Office According to a notice from the Enban International Telegraph Association Office: The Czech Ministry of Posts and Telecommunications has formulated a list of telegraph office names in the country written in Czech. From January 1 this year, telegrams sent to the Czech Republic whose recipient place names are not sent according to the list of office names above will be returned to the sender and handled as undeliverable. This rule only applies to international telegrams, and the list of office names compiled in German or Hungarian will still be used for domestic telegrams in the country. (The Ministry of Communications has also received this notice and has informed all offices in December last year.)

Connection of Japan-US Wireless Telephone Overseas telephone services in the United States have connected US telephone agencies with major cities in Japan (Tokyo, West Kyoto, Yokohama, Kobe) for direct calls since December 7 last year. There are nearly one million Japanese phones, making it the 60th country within the range of the American frequency, and it will become an important country in the world communications network. The United States is actually in a central position in this communications network. Of the countries that have not communicated with the United States and have 100,000 phones, only New Zealand, Soviet Russia, and China have that distinction.

Super-Scientific Divination 298

— Qiongsheng

When the world is in chaos, Chinese fortune-tellers often use phrases like "good fortune follows bad" or "Heaven is not tired of chaos, and it is inevitable" to cater to people's desire for peace. Even scholars like to talk about "King Wen's Divine Lesson" and brag about divination with tortoise shells and yarrow stalks. The well-known Zhuge Kongming was greatly skilled in "observing celestial phenomena, understanding geography, mastering yin and yang, and understanding numerology," and was truly able to "hold the universe in his sleeves." In this way, the life, death, survival, or destruction of ordinary people all depend on fate. There is no other reason besides fate.

Now, the universe is shouting about economic panic and the threat of war again. Ordinary people's old wounds have not yet healed, and new wounds have reappeared. In addition to being terrified, they cannot find a way to eliminate disasters and avoid calamities on their own, so they flock to fortune-tellers again. As a result, in addition to the thriving careers of some astrologers, the (scientific spirit medium), which is popular both at home and abroad, has become popular. This is why many experts and doctors are able to practice political hypnosis. The Paris Observatory Director Maurice's statement after observing the sun and moon, that sunspots constantly emit electric and magnetic forces that can make people feel uneasy and irritable, thus hiding the great war crisis of 1936 and 1937 and causing other disasters, and citing history to prove his point, saying that the world can enjoy peace and prosperity, and mankind can devote itself to art and culture, when the sun is still, is this kind of (pure) argument.

Using astronomical evidence in science to explain the difficulty of mankind's enjoyment of peace and prosperity and the inevitable arrival of world war is as brilliant as the explanations of the Heavenly Lord of the Primordial Beginning in the Investiture of the Gods, who used (divine will) to explain the inevitable calamities of people, but Maurice claims that he does not believe in astrology, so we might as well call it super-scientific divination. The reason why it is super-scientific is because it has the following meanings.

(1) Since the electric and magnetic forces emitted by sunspots have already made humans irritable and uneasy, thereby concealing the crisis of world war, this is tantamount to saying that (science) has already determined (fate). Because although many scientists are now ascending to the stratosphere and even fantasizing about flying to other planets, they have not yet reached the point where they can eliminate sunspots, or (steal the sky and replace the sun). Knowing that the war is coming, but its coming is determined by the sun, which is beyond the power of us humans, isn't this a very modern (fate)?

(2) Since it is fate, it naturally means that not only is the reduction of armaments and the running around for peace by Laval and others futile, but also that any methods we think of to eliminate war and resist war are useless. In that case, let's all listen to fate and head towards war! Because trying to eliminate war and resist war is no different from violating (science).

(3) Nowadays, heresies are rampant, saying that war is the initiative of a few people, and most people suffer, but since it has been decided by the sun, of course these nonsense are all ghost stories. We can only (unite as one) and head towards war. Saying that it is for the benefit of a few people, and even wanting people to rise up and resist, is too unscientific!

Now is the world of science, science is omnipotent, and countries are sparing no effort to promote science. Being able to achieve such effectiveness is not without reason.
